Four Foreign Aircraft Pilots Detained in Shaanxi

The Great American Evening News said that two German pilots of the Eurasia Aviation Company are still being held in Xi'an by Zhang Xueliang. In addition, Wayne Gager, the chief mechanic of the Hangzhou National Aviation College, and Captain Senis, the German pilot of Chiang Kai-shek's guards, were also detained. Mr. Wei was ordered by the Nanjing aviation authorities to go to Xi'an to repair the plane, and arrived on the morning of the incident, and was detained. It is said that there is no danger, and his wife and children are now living in Hangzhou. Zhang Xueliang also ordered his pilot, an American named Liao Lade, to guard Mr. Wei, so Liao could not leave Xi'an either. When Soong Zi-wen and Mr. Donald's plane arrived in Xi'an, its pilot lived in the same place as the detained foreigners, but was not allowed to talk to them.

Two Party Headquarters Telegraph the Three Commanders-in-Chief in Urgent Terms

The Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Special Party Headquarters, because Zhang rebelled Xueliang committed crimes and caused chaos, hijacked the commander, and the central government has ordered the suppression and commissioned He Yingqin, Minister of Military and Political Affairs, as the commander-in-chief of the rebels' suppression army, and commissioned Liu Zhi and Gu Zhutong as the commanders-in-chief of the eastern and western rebels' suppression armies, all of whom have telegraphed to take office. The command of the west has brought good news, and therefore specially telegraphed to quickly sweep away the rebels and welcome and protect the commander. The original telegram is copied as follows: Urgent, Nanjing Ministry of Military Affairs transferred the rebels' suppression army Commander He, and Commanders Liu and Gu Jianjian. I have heard that Zhang rebels Xueliang hijacked the chairmanship, committed crimes and caused chaos, betrayed the country and colluded with bandits, hoping to destroy unity and subvert the government. The executive chief leads the officers and men, waving tears to start a discussion, and after a long hearing, they admire and comfort me. Two thousand employees of this road vow to support the central government and be the backer of the total seat. Please quickly direct the army to the west, sweep away the rebels, and welcome and protect the commander, so as to revitalize discipline and consolidate the foundation of the country. Telegraf to reply and wait for the good news. Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Ningbo Railway Special Party Headquarters, Koushun.

More Than Two Thousand Young Men in Shanghai County Vow to Rescue the Leader from Danger; Held at the County Government on the Morning of the Day Before Yesterday

According to the Central News Agency, after the Shaanxi Incident occurred, Chiang Kai-shek was in distress. People from all walks of life in Shanghai County were extremely angry. For the past ten days, Zhang Xueliang has not had any sincere repentance, and the leader has not been out of danger. More than 2,500 young men who were trained in the second phase of the county were willing to dedicate their blood and sweat to the central government, rescue the leader, and suppress the rebels. Therefore, at 9:00 AM on the day before yesterday (23rd), all the trained young men in the county, except for the four, five, and three districts that were far away from the county government, gathered at the same time. All the districts should take an oath. In addition, more than 200 young men from the one, three, and two districts gathered in the auditorium of the county government to swear allegiance to the leader. Commissioner Guo Hongxin of the Second District Supervision Commissioner's Office, County Mayor Li Zhifu, and Liu Jiaoguan Shen and others attended the swearing-in ceremony. After the ceremony, Ding Hongzhang, the principal of the First District Civil School, led the young men to read the oath, which said, "We swear to be sincere and support the leader, and we are willing to dedicate our blood and sweat to the central government, suppress the rebels, and rescue the leader from danger. From the day we take the oath, we are willing to bear the responsibility of rescuing the leader from danger under the unified leadership and command of the central government. Even if we go through fire and water, we will never lag behind. We will never stop until we achieve our goal. This oath." After the oath was taken, Commissioner Guo Hongzhi gave a training speech first, followed by County Mayor Li Zhifu and Liu Jiaoguan Shen, who gave training speeches one after another. The words all encouraged the young men to support the leader and be loyal to the central government, especially when County Mayor Li Zhifu gave a detailed explanation of the Xi'an Incident and Zhang rebel's past behaviors. The words were extremely indignant. The atmosphere in the whole place was very tense, and the emotions were extremely enthusiastic. Finally, Principal Ding led the crowd to shout slogans: (1) Chiang Kai-shek is our only leader, (2) Chiang Kai-shek is the savior of our country, (3) Chiang Kai-shek is the teacher of our people's revival, (4) We must revive the nation, and we must first rescue Chairman Wei from danger, (5) We must save the country, and we must first eliminate the rebels, (6) We must swear to rescue Chairman Wei from danger, (7) Support the leader, (8) Support the central government, (9) Long live the Three Principles of the People, (10) Long live the Republic of China, and other slogans, and then they all returned to their teams at about 11:00.

The End of the National Calendar Year Approaches; Silver and Money Businesses Provide Loans to Facilitate Various Industries; Businesses Have Begun Year-End Account Closings; Holiday Today, Resuming Transactions the Following Day

As the end of December in the national calendar nears, silver and money businesses are starting to close their accounts and are also trying their best to provide loans to facilitate various industries. Today is the Yunnan Uprising Memorial Day, and both Chinese and foreign banks are closed for the day. Detailed information is provided below:

Silver and Money Businesses: Account Closings

Account closings for banks are typically done at the end of June and December. Currently, various banks have started calculating interest for savings deposits on the 20th. Interest calculations for commercial deposits and debts will begin today, with the year-end final account closings scheduled for the end of the month. The Bankers' Association has scheduled a regular meeting of its members for 4 PM on the 29th. Account closings for money businesses are traditionally done at the end of the lunar year; however, starting this year, they will also be done once at the end of the national calendar year. Various firms are already complying. The Money Business Association has scheduled a members' representative meeting for 2 PM on the 31st.

Firms Provide Loans to Facilitate Various Industries

Agricultural products in various regions have had bumper harvests this year, making various industries vibrant, especially the cotton textile industry. Banks and money businesses have generally tightened various loans, both secured and unsecured. However, since the autumn of this year, they have changed their previous methods and have been particularly lenient in providing loans, aiming to facilitate various industries. Loan interest rates have also been slightly reduced compared to the past. Therefore, it is expected that various industries will weather the year steadily without any other concerns.

Holiday Today, Resuming Transactions the Following Day

Today is the Yunnan Uprising Memorial Day and Christmas Day. Member banks of the Bankers' Association are closed for the day according to the holiday schedule. At the same time, affiliated institutions such as the bank clearing house and the bank acceptance house are also closed. The Money Business Association issued a notice stating, "The 25th of this month is the Yunnan Uprising Memorial Day. All member firms and the money business reserve will be closed for the day. Transactions scheduled for today will be processed the following day. This is hereby announced." Foreign banks are also closed for the day.

City Party and Government Organs Jointly Issue Notice to Prevent Labor Unrest; Labor and Management Should Share Hardships; No Wage Cuts, No Negligence

The city party headquarters and the city government believe that during this time of national crisis, it is especially important to maintain local order. To prevent labor unrest and avoid disputes, they jointly issued a notice yesterday stating, "Given the current national crisis, local order is extremely important. Labor and management in all industries should share hardships and maintain their livelihoods without causing disputes. This committee (government) is jointly issuing this notice to prevent labor unrest and maintain local security. It is hoped that employers in all industries will uphold the overall situation and not take this opportunity to cut wages or lay off workers, so as not to provide ammunition for critics. Workers in all industries should also not arbitrarily neglect their duties or go on strike. Both sides should uphold a spirit of mutual assistance and resolve disputes amicably. Any lawless individuals who incite labor unrest and endanger order will be immediately and severely arrested without leniency. Everyone must strictly comply and avoid transgressions. This is the notice."

Public Security Bureau Intensifies Anti-Drug Propaganda; Second Day's Situation

Since the Public Security Bureau of this city intensified anti-drug propaganda on the 23rd, the workload has been particularly intense. Yesterday (the 24th) was the second day of propaganda. The bureau assigned propaganda workers to continue organizing propaganda teams in batches according to designated areas and set out to spread awareness. The hours were from 9 AM to 12 PM in the morning and 2 PM to 5 PM in the afternoon. In the morning, special attention was paid to vegetable markets, tea houses, and other places. In the afternoon, they mostly went to game venues, other factories, and public places. The propaganda methods used were (1) door-to-door persuasion, (2) speeches, and (3) posting or distributing propaganda materials. It is said that the bureau is also planning to hold a large-scale parade in the near future. The main points of this propaganda campaign are roughly four: (1) Advise those who use strong drugs to quickly quit on their own within this year. (2) Advise those who manufacture and sell drugs to change their profession as soon as possible. (3) Advise landlords and sub-landlords not to rent houses to people who manufacture, sell, or use drugs. (4) Provide a detailed explanation of other harms of drugs and the severity of the punishments under the Provisional Regulations on Prohibiting Drugs and Punishing Drug Crimes for propaganda purposes. At the same time, they are checking door-to-door to urge smokers who have not renewed their licenses to quickly renew their third-term smoking cessation licenses.

Anniversary of Tang Youren's Death; His Relatives and Friends Chanting Sutras Today; Inscription of Epitaph Personally Written by Wang Jingwei

The late Central Committee member Tang Youren was assassinated at his residence in Shanghai on December 25th of last year. Today is the anniversary of his death. Due to the Xi'an Incident, Tang's family did not want to make a big show. Initiated by relatives and friends, they are chanting sutras in commemoration at the Huguo Chan Temple on Mengdelan Road in the British Concession of this city, without holding any other ceremony. The epitaph written by Chairman Wang was sent some time ago. The original text is recorded below:

(Epitaph for Mr. Youren) Mr. Tang Youren, whose given name was Lin and used his courtesy name, was assassinated at his residence in Shanghai on December 25th of the 24th year of the Republic. He was buried in the Wanguo Public Cemetery in western Shanghai in February of the following year. His family and friends entrusted Zhao Ming with the responsibility of writing the epitaph. I, Zhao Ming, respectfully note that Mr. Tang's given name was Lin, and he used his courtesy name. He was born on the 20th day of the sixth month of the year Jiawu in the 18th year before the Republic, in Xixiang, Liuyang, Hunan. His grandfather's name was Xianchou, courtesy name Shoutian, a famous person in the county, known for his filial piety. His father's name was Caichang, courtesy name Fochen, who died for the cause in Ezhou during the Gengzi Rebellion. His younger brother, Cichen, also died for the cause in Changsha. The heroism of their deaths is recorded in history. Mr. Tang was only seven years old at that time. Mr. Shoutian was poor, but he spared no effort to raise his grandchildren, and he provided food and clothing to revolutionaries who were in danger. His lofty character and sincere actions are detailed in the Biography of Tang Taigong of Liuyang by Xiao Peigen of Taoyuan. Mr. Tang received education from his grandfather when young. From Gengzi to Jiyou, he lived in exile for ten years. During this time, he once went to Japan with his elder brother Guiliang, and entered the Shanghai Sanyu School with his younger brother Bunian. He returned in Gengxu and studied at the Hunan Higher Industrial School. In Xinhai, the Wuchang Uprising occurred, and Jiao Dafeng, Chen Zuoxin, Li Xigui, and other party members responded in Changsha. Mr. Tang was deeply involved in the events. After the first year of the Republic, he studied in Japan, graduating from Keio University in the eighth year. After returning to China, he assisted his brother Guiliang in founding the Yangtze Daily in Hankou. The following year, he traveled north and worked at the Bank of China. Mr. Tang had long specialized in economics and finance, and at this time, he devoted himself to examining the national situation, gaining profound insights. He also worked as a university professor and wrote articles for newspapers, expressing his accumulated knowledge. He was knowledgeable and insightful. The Modern Review, published by Wang Shijie, Zhou Gengsheng, Yang Duanliu, Ding Xielin, and others, was particularly valued by the world. In the 20th year, he was elected as an alternate member of the Central Executive Committee at the Fourth National Congress of the Chinese Kuomintang. In the 21st year, he served as the Secretary-General of the Central Political Council in the party headquarters, and as a member of the Legislative Yuan in the government. He then served as the Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. At the Fifth National Congress in the 20th year, he was elected as a member of the Central Executive Committee and transferred to the position of Vice Minister of the Ministry of Transportation. During these years, although the country was in deep crisis, Mr. Tang devoted himself to his duties. He particularly worked tirelessly day and night in diplomacy, seeking ways to save the nation. He firmly believed in and adhered to the teachings of Sun Yat-sen regarding the world situation and Sino-Japanese relations. He did his best to implement the decisions of the party headquarters and the government, not avoiding hardship, and not caring about doubts and slanders. China had been weak for a long time, and it was compounded by years of war and chaos. The threat from abroad was imminent. Responding with recklessness would only harm the life of the nation, while enduring with patience would harm the nation's dignity. National strength is accumulated bit by bit and cannot be achieved overnight. Sacrifice cannot be based on empty words. The anxiety in his heart and the depth of his worries could not be fully understood by everyone. His assassination may have been due to the fact that in recent years, he had been constantly concerned about survival and danger. As a negotiator, he could not avoid disappointing some people, which led to this. However, Mr. Tang had long put reputation, life, and death aside. Mr. Tang died at the age of only forty-two. The National Government issued an order to commend his loyalty and gave generous compensation to his family. His wife was Ouyang, the granddaughter of Mr. Ouyang. His sons, Youcheng and Mancheng, and his three daughters, Liancheng, were all young. Mr. Tang was sincere by nature. When his father, Mr. Fochen, entrusted himself to national affairs, he never forgot it. He often told Zhao Ming about the recovery of Changsha in Xinhai, feeling comforted by the fact that he could carry on his father's ambitions. He said that his mother had wept blood for more than ten years, but now she could finally smile for her children. When Mr. Tang was studying in Tokyo, Mr. Huang Xing saw his youthful and vigorous spirit and said with joy and sorrow, "Fochen has an heir, that is for sure." Mr. Tang's actions during his life are detailed in his biography written by his younger brother Bunian, and in the biographical sketch written by his friend Huang Jun. Here, I summarize the major events to mark his grave. Written by Zhao Ming with respect.

Portrait of Mr. Tang Youren

The Dahua Ship Ran Aground But Was Rescued; Shuangqiyang Waters Near Dinghai; Passengers and Crew Rescued and Arrived in Dinghai

The Dahua ship, owned by the Ping'an Steamship Company and operating on the Shanghai-Taiwan route, weighed 1,071.19 tons, was 199 feet long, 29 feet 1 inch wide, and 18 feet 2 inches deep, with a draft of 13 feet and a speed of 10 nautical miles per hour. On the evening of the 22nd, it departed from Haimen with more than 300 passengers and a large amount of cargo, heading to Shanghai via Shipu, Dinghai, Chuanshan, and other places. At 4 AM on the 23rd, when it reached the Shuangqiyang waters, 60 nautical miles from Dinghai, it suddenly encountered thick fog, causing it to steer off course.

Accidentally Hit a Reef

The ship ran aground on a reef. The area is full of hidden reefs, and the mountain foot extends into the sea. When the ship hit the reef, the hull shook violently. The stern was broken by the reef, and the bottom of the rear hold cracked, allowing seawater to immediately enter. All passengers on board were extremely frightened. The captain urgently sent a distress signal, which was received by the Nanhai ship sailing between Ningbo and Haimen. The Nanhai ship immediately rushed to the Shuangqiyang waters to rescue the Dahua ship. The Nanhai ship anchored in the open sea and launched lifeboats to the Dahua ship. They managed to first rescue all the passengers, more than 300 people, and some of the crew,

Rescued in Succession

and transferred them to the Nanhai ship, which then sailed to Ningbo. They arrived safely in Ningbo yesterday morning. After receiving the telegram from the captain of the Dahua ship, the manager of the Shanghai head office, Li Yaoting, took the Chuanshan ship to Dinghai to assess the situation and prepare for rescue. As there are many pirates in the area and the ship still had cargo, the ship's accountant first arranged for local military police in Dinghai to

Send Ships for Protection

in case of emergency. Although the rear hold was flooded after the ship ran aground, the hull was supported by the reef and did not sink immediately. The first and second holds are said to be intact.

The Red Cross Transports a Large Number of Medicines to Suiyuan Yesterday; Representatives from Shanxi Come to Shanghai to Collect Them; Yan Fuqing Receives Reports from Suiyuan

Since the Suiyuan Incident occurred, the local association of the Chinese Red Cross in this city, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and other organizations jointly formed the Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Relief and慰劳Committee, and sent representatives to the front lines to inquire about needed supplies. Yesterday, the committee transported a large number of medicines to General Fu. At the same time, Mr. Yan Fuqing received letters from the front lines reporting on the situation in Suiyuan. Details are provided below:

Special Train Transports to Suiyuan Li Hongwen, the representative of the Taiyuan Pacification Commissioner's Office stationed in Nanjing, sent his son to Shanghai yesterday to collect medicines from the Relief Committee of the Red Cross Society of China. The committee immediately handed over 87,750 packages of first-aid and other medicines, totaling 186 pieces, which were transported to the front lines by several specially prepared train cars attached to two routes for delivery to General Fu. At the same time, the Red Cross Society of China also transported 5,000 packages of injectable medicines and first-aid medicines to the Suiyuan Branch of the Red Cross and the North China Temporary Branch of the Relief Committee for use. According to the association, it has been repeatedly receiving telegrams from the front lines stating that various supplies are urgently needed, and they still hope that all sectors will continue to donate generously.

Reports from the Front Lines Yesterday, Mr. Yan Fuqing received a letter from Dr. Sang Pei'en of the Guisui Mongolian Health Institute, reporting on the situation in Suiyuan. The original letter stated, (omitted above) "The Military Medical Department sent the entire staff of the Fifth Temporary Hospital to Suiyuan the day before yesterday. The hospital is quite large and can accommodate 500 people. Four doctors from Peking Union Medical College have come to assist, so there is no immediate shortage of medical personnel. However, there is still a shortage of medical supplies. I wonder if the General Society can find a way to supplement them. All the lightly wounded soldiers have gradually recovered, and the seriously wounded have also improved. During this period, I am deeply afraid that the wounded soldiers will engage in irregular activities and seek entertainment. Therefore, local colleagues have asked me to solicit various legitimate entertainment items from Shanghai, such as various old books, newspapers, magazines, educational chess pieces, and other game items to relieve boredom. There must be many enthusiastic men and women in Shanghai who are willing to donate. Both new and old items, regardless of type, are very welcome and can be sent directly to the Army-Civilian Joint Entertainment Society, or handed over to me for transfer. It is reported that women in various places are rushing to knit woolen sweaters and other items for the soldiers on the front lines, which is really touching to see the patriotic enthusiasm of the women, but these are not suitable for this place outside the Great Wall. In addition to the large leather jackets and pants produced locally, (large fur coats cost about five yuan each) other cotton and woolen items are not enough to keep out the cold, etc."

Customs Brokers Association Held a General Meeting Yesterday to Oppose Weighing Goods; Calculating and Paying Waterpower Based on Declared Weight; Shanghai Native Place Associations Association Will Hold a Meeting

Da Gong She reports that regarding the proposal by the six shipping companies to weigh heavy goods by the Pingzhun Company and charge waterpower based on the weighed tonnage, the Shanghai Native Place Associations Association has published an objection in the newspaper on behalf of the Transportation and Customs Brokers Association. The six companies have also invited Wu Yongxia, a representative of the Native Place Associations Association, and Chen Panjun, a representative of the Customs Brokers Association, to hold a joint meeting at the Shipping Club. It is reported that the Yangtze River branch of the Customs Brokers Association held a general meeting of all members yesterday to discuss the case. Everyone unanimously insisted on calculating and paying waterpower based on the declared and taxed weight, refusing to recognize the weighing by the Pingzhun Company, believing that calculating based on customs weight is fair to all parties. Among the six companies, the three Chinese companies are closer to the customer associations and the customs brokers, and they should uphold the spirit of Chinese business cooperation. Although the idea of promoting domestic goods was expressed with some dissent in the meeting, foreign companies have always set lower waterpower rates for foreign goods than for domestic goods, which shows the intention of foreign merchants to maintain foreign goods. Compared to that, domestic goods are already at a disadvantage in waterpower rates, but Chinese companies have not paid attention to this. Now, a new rule is being created, which seems excessive. No wonder customer associations and customs brokers insist on opposing it. It is also learned that the customer association also plans to convene a meeting within a few days. If it is found out which company initiated the case, they will first try to deal with it in the hope that they will reflect on it.

Chinese and Foreign Banks Cooperate to Maintain Foreign Exchange Successfully; Finance Minister Kong Thanks Foreign Merchants

Xin Sheng She reports that since the Xi'an Incident, foreign exchange transactions at the Central, Bank of China, and Communications Bank suddenly increased. At that time, the three banks held a meeting and tried their best to maintain stability. With the cooperation and assistance of the British HSBC and other banks, the foreign exchange transactions continued to be bought and sold without limitation by the three banks based on the past policy of stabilizing foreign exchange. Now that the incident has gradually eased, foreign exchange transactions have returned to their previous state. The daily exchange rate quoted by the Central Bank is one shilling and two and a half pence for the British pound and thirty US dollars for the US dollar, which is the same as the previously set standard. Minister of Finance and Governor of the Central Bank Kong Xiangxi expressed his gratitude to the foreign banks for their kind cooperation and assistance.

Noodles Industry Association Sent Representatives to Petition Yesterday; Social Affairs Bureau Agreed to Provide Relief

Due to the recent high price of wheat and the low price of rice, the price of flour has more than doubled, which has greatly affected the business of the machine-made noodles industry in this city. It has been difficult to maintain the livelihood of the industry across the city. The Social Affairs Bureau was previously submitted to twice, requesting to suppress the price. Now, because the price of flour and wheat is still rising, the members' meeting again resolved the day before yesterday to nominate Wang Gangwen, Xu Jinfa, Wu Jingeng, etc., to represent the entire industry to petition the Social Affairs Bureau. Yesterday, the representatives took the petition to the bureau to petition. The director sent a clerk, Mr. Song Zhongqing, to receive them. In addition to submitting the petition, Wang Jinwen verbally requested four goals on behalf of the association: (1) Flour is essential to the staple food of civilians. The price increase not only affects the industry's business but also causes panic among civilians across Shanghai. (2) Request to order restrictions on wheat prices, which must not be higher than rice prices. (3) Request to set the price of wheat at no more than six yuan per dan (石) and the price of flour at no more than three yuan per bag. (4) Strictly order the market operating flour and wheat not to monopolize and raise prices. Mr. Song fully accepted the four requests and replied to the representatives that the principles of your association's petition are nothing more than two methods: addressing the symptoms and addressing the root cause. I will convey this to the director and ask to convene a meeting of flour and wheat merchants, such as the Flour Exchange, flour manufacturers, and the Grain Exchange, to discuss relief measures. The representatives were satisfied and returned,

Sujia Railway to Join Through Transport Starting New Year's Day, Approved by Order of the Ministry of Railways

Since the Sujia Railway officially opened for business on July 15 of this year, all previous through transport of passengers and goods on the Nanjing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways and domestic through transport, which had to pass through Shanghai, now have a shortcut to pass through. Merchants and travelers are unwilling to detour again. Therefore, for the sake of economical and convenient vehicle operation, it is necessary for the railway to join the domestic through transport. It was approved by the Ministry of Railways to first join the domestic through transport from January 1, 26th year of the Republic. However, it is only used as a transit route for passenger and freight through transport and does not handle the departure and arrival of goods. Detailed measures have also been formulated separately and submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval under Instruction Lian Zi No. 10917.

The Japanese Naval Landing Forces stationed in Shanghai are scheduled to hold their final exercise of the year at dawn on the 26th, in conjunction with the landing forces of various ships anchored in Shanghai. The area includes the Hongkou area and the industrial areas in eastern and western Shanghai.

Gao Qifeng's Coffin Transported to Beijing

After the public memorial service yesterday, the spirit was moved. After the death of revolutionary pioneer Gao Qifeng, people from all walks of life held a public memorial service at the Chinese Funeral Home on Haig Road at 3 p.m. yesterday. At 4 p.m., the spirit was moved and transported to Beijing for public burial. The details are as follows.

Yesterday's Public Memorial Service

At 3 p.m. yesterday, people from all walks of life held a public memorial service at the Chinese Funeral Home. Mayor Wu Tiecheng (represented by Li Dachao), Ye Gongchuo, Li Dachao, and others, more than 100 people, attended. Gao's adopted daughter, Zhang Kunyi, hosted. At 4 p.m., the spirit was moved, departing from the Haig Road Funeral Home, passing through Fuxu Road, Aiduoya Road. Yu Qiaqing Road, Zhejiang Road, Haining Road. Jielu and reached the North Station. At 6 p.m., it was attached to the Shanghai-Wuxi train and arrived in Wuxi at 1 o'clock. At 6 a.m. this morning, it was transferred to the Wuxi-Beijing train and transported to Beijing. It is expected to arrive in Nanjing at 10 a.m. this morning.

Coffin Transported to Beijing

The public burial ceremony of Gao was originally scheduled for the 20th of this month, but due to insufficient time, it was postponed for a week and rescheduled for the 27th. After the coffin arrives in Beijing, it will be placed at Qixia Mountain. The Beijing office has already arranged a temporary auditorium and opened two large ones for people from all walks of life to pay their respects. At 2 p.m. on the 27th, people from all walks of life in Beijing will hold a public memorial service. At 3 p.m., a public burial will be held in the tomb at Qixia Mountain.

National Government's Memorial Address

The National Government's memorial address to Gao stated, "Oh, Mr., the essence of the art world, your hand chose the sun and moon, your spirit walked thunder and lightning, young and intelligent, older and more mature, looking down at Yuexiu, responding to Wenxing, wherever the pen was dipped, fame filled hundreds of cities, initially assisting the revolution, not envious or greedy, the humble residence was bleak, unmatched in cunning, the rivers and mountains entered the painting, the heavenly wind was in the building, cherish this small painting, there will be thousands of autumns later, the words are common in Zhi Xing, human relations are handsome and resourceful, Feng Huan burned the coupons, Mo Bu worked in poetry, the gains from his spare time, benefited relatives and friends, clear standards and festivals, pine and frost posture, once traveled to foreign lands, men and women competed to see, curly beards and green eyes, Luo Bai clothes, Chinese and Western encompassed, became a wave, Dan Qing's superb art, those who saw it were amazed, they thought it was a chaste trunk, withered after the cold year, the high mountain was admired, hundreds of waters came to the dynasty, its steps were proud, its vision was clear, Europe and Asia jointly carried great pride, how could it be expected that in the middle way, this master craftsman would be lost, the golden rooster records the year, the jade tree is destroyed by the wind, the scholars mourn, the fine arts will be exhausted, zero slices of paper, young works into long rainbows, alas, the country cherishes exhaustion, the hub government is annoyed, remembering the name and virtue, planting people for a hundred years, raw grass to offer sacrifices, spring flowers to be placed at the banquet, the soul returns, Jiang Ze is eternally continuous, alas, Xiang,"

Public Burial Organization

The organization of the Public Burial Committee of Mr. Gao Qifeng is as follows: (1) Painting Saint Gao Qifeng Niu Sheng Yilao's party and country, exhausted his strength in aesthetics, said sincerity, did not serve as an official or marry, the festival was like Jie Tui, the character was high like Liu Hui, the actions were clear as the sun and moon, the learning was through adults, the Prime Minister always called him moving and honest, the people of the country all praised him for his noble and clean, he was sent to Berlin two years ago, unfortunately died on the way, and the National Government had ordered him to be commended, paid for the funeral, and prepared his life deeds and academic works to be deposited in the historical museum for publication. Colleagues and others recently submitted a petition to publicly bury his remains in the capital, which was also approved by the National Government and the Executive Yuan, respectively, informing us by letter. Therefore, the Public Burial Committee of Mr. Gao Qifeng was established to handle the selection of land, welcoming the coffin, and public burial matters. (2) This association is organized by several members. The petitioner who submits the petition for relocation to Beijing for public burial is a natural member. (3) This association is located at No. 48 Beiping Road, New Residential Area, Capital (within the Sino-French Friendship Association) (4) This association establishes a director-general, secretary, staff, and coffin-welcoming commissioner, who are appointed by the members.

Hengfeng Road, Fire Kills and Injures Three, Destroys Eight City Buildings

The Yuyuanlong New Clothing Store at No. 27 South Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, suddenly caught fire for unknown reasons at around 3 a.m. yesterday. When the people in the store found out, the stairs were already on fire and they could not escape. Therefore, the store owner Wu Rongfu, his wife Zhu, and his apprentice, etc., all jumped from the balcony along the road. His young son, named Fu Yuan, 10 years old, was buried in the fire because he could not be rescued, and was burned to a crisp. The second son, named Yu Yuan, also injured his head, hands, and feet, etc. The fire brigades of various sections drove to the scene with ambulances and sent him to the hospital. Wu Rongfu injured his head, face, hands, and feet, and was bandaged at the hospital. When the fire was raging, the northwest wind was very strong, so the flames spread southward, so in addition to the Yuanfa Noodle Shop at No. 20, the adjacent building to the north, the rest of the buildings facing south were burned, including the Xu Rongsheng Guangi Store at No. 115, the Xingyangtai Tobacco and Paper Store at No. 23, the Yimin Printing Factory at No. 21, the Congee Shop at No. 19, the Zou Jinji New Clothing Store at No. 17, and the Xiangyu Wine Store at No. 15, a total of eight city buildings. The back is a silk factory, fortunately the walls were high and it was not affected, which is also fortunate. After the disaster, the police at Post No. 7 of the Hengfeng Road Police Station at the site ran to the station to report the incident. The director of the station, Pei, dispatched senior police officers to the scene to suppress the situation, so the order was still good. Later, the arsonist Wu Rongfu was taken to the station. According to the confession, the fire started on the escalator. I was already fast asleep at the time, so I didn't know where the fire came from. However, my store had fire insurance of 2,000 yuan, etc. As for the boy Wu Fuyuan who was burned to death, yesterday the local guarantor Shen Xiaowu reported to the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy. In the late afternoon, prosecutor Hu Songshu, etc., arrived at the scene and found that the dead boy Wu Fuyuan had indeed died from burns. The local guarantor was ordered to prepare a coffin for the family to collect and bury the body themselves. The arsonist Wu Rongfu was sent to the Public Security Bureau for joint interrogation at around 5 p.m. yesterday. Also yesterday afternoon, a firewood shop warehouse behind Linfengli, at the intersection of Huasheng Road and Xinmin Road in Zhabei, was also careless with fire, and a thick smoke filled the air. The fire engines of various sections rushed to the scene to rescue and put out the fire, spreading to many Jiangbei thatched sheds in the area. It took about two hours to put out the fire. The arsonist Chen Wenxiang, 40 years old, from Shaoxing, was arrested. It is said that he is the old steward of the machine room.

Therefore, 72 residents including Tao Menghua, Tao Qinwen, Tao Hongcan, and Zhang Zhenqi have jointly submitted a petition to the Municipal Government, the Municipal Public Works Bureau, and the Labor Service Committee, requesting dredging. Yesterday, the Municipal Government replied that the Zhen River section will be dredged together with the East-West Zhujia Ditch. The representatives were afraid that if they were dredged together, they would be invaded by tides, and drinking water and farmland would not be suitable. Judge Zhong Qing ordered that he remain in custody and the case be rescheduled for seven days to investigate and verify further.

Yu Wenlin Sues for False Imprisonment; Xing Zhigang and Others Not Guilty; Yu's Transfer to Xiqin Institute Was an Administrative Punishment; Lawsuit Invalid, Should Appeal to Higher Authority

Xing Zhigang, the district chief of the fifth district of Chenjiaxing Town in Pudong, Shanghai County, Shi Konghuai, the secretary of the Shanghai Municipal Council's Public Utilities Bureau, Gao Shu'an, the deputy director of the Wharf Management Office, and Wang Jun, an inspector, were sued by Yu Wenlin, also known as Yu A-si, in the local court by Zhou Yingjie and Zhou Yingcai, two lawyers. Xing Zhigang, in the name of the shipping association, allegedly instigated Wang Jun to arrest Yu and take him to the Wharf Management Office, from where Gao Shu'an sent him to the Caoxi River vagrant labor institution via Shi Konghuai, falsely accusing him of

Collecting Illegal Fees

at the wharf.

However, the plaintiff claims to be a watchman hired by various shipping companies, exchanging labor for money, and requests that the defendants be punished for false imprisonment and defamation, and that he be released from the institution. He was summoned for questioning, but because Yu was still at the institute, the court ordered a postponement. Yesterday, Judge Yu Lude continued the trial, with the official arguing from the plaintiff's lawyer's statement that, "This morning, the court ordered the bailiff to go to the Xiqin Institute to bring Yu Wenlin, but they have not been able to bring him yet. According to the bailiff, he can only be brought at noon. Now, let us first question the defendants."

Shi Minhuai Testified:

Age 39, from Haimen, Secretary of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau and concurrently the Director of the Wharf Management Office, residing at 92 Longmen Village. I am responsible for the wharf warehouse. Daily and special matters are handled by the Director of the Bureau. On September 9th at 10 a.m., Deputy Director Gao Shu'an called me, saying that Inspector Wang Jun, along with wharf policeman Ning Haisheng, found Yu Wenlin collecting night watch insurance fees at the Gongyi Wharf, and also found a stub book showing that he had collected from

More than Sixty Establishments

Totaling over one hundred dollars. Because this violated Article 16 of the Wharf Regulations, Vice Director Gao and Wang Jun brought him to the Management Office. Yu admitted his wrongdoing, so according to Article 7 of the Wharf Regulations, he was sent to the Vagrant Labor Institute. At this point, Gao Shu'an testified that after bringing in Yu, they found that Yu had committed a criminal offense before, as proven by a letter from the Yangjing Security Corps. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that, regarding the information in the Security Corps' letter, the plaintiff had stated that the Security Corps had

Falsely Accused Him of Theft

and that the High Court had acquitted him, so this evidence is not credible. At this point, the official ordered that Yu Wenlin be brought in and the trial would resume at 2 p.m. In the afternoon, after Yu Wenlin was brought in, Judge Yu continued the trial with all defendants present. Yu Wenlin, also known as Yu A-si, testified that he was 42 years old, from Dongtai, residing at 52 Laobaidu, Pudong, had previously rowed boats, and that since June 20th of this year, he has been working as a night watchman for ships, not insurance, but rather that the wharf owners at Gongyi Wharf

Voluntarily Paid

him. This small book is mine, and the one hundred plus dollars in it are what the ship owners gave me, one or two dollars each. I have no grudges against the Wharf Management Office, the local inspectors, or Xing Zhigang. That day, Inspector Wang called me ashore and immediately arrested me and took me to the Management Office, and sent me to the Xiqin Institute. At this point, Xing Zhigang testified that someone was impersonating me and extorting money from ship owners. The water patrol team wrote to me, saying they had captured Yu A-si. I said not to deal with it. I am the district chief, I have no time to advise. At this point, the official began the debate. The defendant's lawyer, Li Zuyu, argued that one could collect over two hundred dollars in insurance fees per month, and that there would be danger if one did not pay, so it can be seen that it was

Not Voluntary.

Moreover, this punishment, based on the management regulations, sent him to the Vagrant Labor Institute for rehabilitation, not imprisonment. The lawsuit is therefore invalid. The judge declared the debate closed and announced the verdict that the defendants were all not guilty. Yu Wenlin was sent back to the Xiqin Institute, and it was ordered that this was an administrative punishment and could only be appealed to the higher authorities of the original punishment. The lawsuit was not legal. The court then adjourned.

Disputes Arise Again at Longhua Temple; Ten Directions Monks Accuse Yuanming; Accuse Yuanming of Controlling Temple Property with Secretive Actions; Allege Buddhist Instruments, Religious Items, and Silk Fabrics All Sold Off; Chinese Buddhist Association Sends Letter to Shanghai Branch for Handling

Longhua Temple in this city is a famous ancient temple. Since the former abbot, Yuanzhao, was accused of selling temple property by the succeeding abbot, Xingkong, a lawsuit arose in the Shanghai Local Court and disputes occurred repeatedly. This year, Xingkong resigned again, and the temple elected Yuanming to succeed him. In September of this year, the Shanghai Buddhist Association went to take over, but this did not materialize. Now, more than ten monks from the ten directions, including Yueqiao, have filed a complaint with the Chinese Buddhist Association accusing Yuanming of controlling temple property. The association has forwarded it to the Shanghai Buddhist Association for handling together. The Datong News Agency reporter has recorded the original complaint and official letter below.

Monk Yueqiao, et al., Submit a Complaint

A document from the ten-direction monks Yueqiao et al. to the Chinese Buddhist Association states: "Regarding the matter of an inferior monk controlling the temple, which has become bankrupt, requesting a ruling for relief. Longhua Temple is an ancient temple of thousands of years. Since Xingkong retreated and requested that your Association elect a worthy successor, Yuanming and a group of Sichuan monks have taken the position of abbot and expelled monks from other provinces who were staying there. The ten-direction monastery has become the private property of Sichuan people, and their conduct speaks for itself. Yueqiao and others further investigated the temple and found that its actions were secretive, disorderly, and

Refused to Accept the Abbot Selected by Your Association, Rejecting them twice and resorting to violence at every turn, making their arrogance evident. Yueqiao and others, as members of the Longhua staff and as Buddhists, could not bear to sit idly by for the sake of preserving the ancient temple of thousands of years, and were therefore compelled to speak out. Hereby, they present a list of their illegal actions and the bankruptcy situation, as stated on the left: (1) Closing the mountain gate tightly and secretly constructing hidden doors behind the abbot's residence and the supervisor's residence, making their whereabouts secretive. (2) The temple's property has all been mortgaged. The temple rooms east of the gate are mortgaged to the residents. (3) They have entered into contracts with people to privately sell the temple's annual income from tin foil, fire wax, and candles. (4) All the solemn religious instruments in the temple have been pawned. (5) A set of red satin embroidered Buddha canopies, four in total, worth five to six hundred dollars, donated by layman Zhang Xiaolin, have already been pawned, along with hundreds of beds, Buddhist instruments, religious items, bronze stoves, and many vestments used for Buddhist ceremonies, as well as furniture items, and wooden items purchased for over one thousand and forty dollars during this year's precepts period, all have been pawned and sold off, and hidden elsewhere. What is the intention behind these actions? Are they intentionally planning to abscond with the temple's funds, or do they have other intentions? It is difficult to guess. Longhua is an ancient temple of thousands of years, a monastery of the ten directions, now being ravaged and plundered by Yuanming and the supervisor Xinghui. Not only is it destroying the Buddha Dharma, but it is also harming public morals day by day. We petition that your Association, as the highest group and organization of Buddhism, is responsible for guiding and protecting the Buddha Dharma and temple property. Therefore, we humbly request that your Association promptly send personnel to investigate and refer the matter to government agencies for legal sanctions to maintain the temple property and protect the ancient temple. The merit is immeasurable. Presented to the Chinese Buddhist Association. Presented by the representatives of the ten directions, Shengzhi, Yueqiao, Bensen, Cizheng, Yongjian, Manyue, Zhikai, Hongjing, Benwu, Guangli, Shanxiang, Ruhai, Shiyin, Yuansheng, Zhihui, Yuxiu, Ji Hui."

Chinese Buddhist Association Letter

According to the submission of the Chinese Buddhist Association, a public letter to the Shanghai Buddhist Association states: "The Chairman has forwarded a complaint from Monk Yueqiao, et al., and Lu Mingzhao, the representative of the Longhua Temple's Shan Lord, regarding the inferior monk occupying Longhua, selling off temple property, and requesting a ruling for relief, etc. The Longhua Temple incident is currently being handled by your Association, and we believe you should copy the original complaint and send it for reference, and we hope that you will report the handling situation to this Association at any time. This is addressed to the Shanghai Branch, Secretariat of the Chinese Buddhist Association."

American Trading Company Representative to Arrive in Shanghai Soon; Will Purchase as Many Chinese Goods for Export as Possible

Mr. Leo Jesfsberg, a famous merchant from New York, is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on January 5th of next year. He is the general manager of the American Trading Company, a well-known firm in New York. The company is a joint venture between Mr. Jessberg and Mr. Greenberg and is now one of the largest importing firms in the United States. Its branch offices are located all over the world. In addition to purchasing all kinds of goods manufactured in various parts of the world in large quantities, the company is also happy to be the first to introduce any new products suitable for sale in the US and Canadian markets to people in those countries. Therefore, the company is not only an importer but also an entrepreneur. Mr. Jessberg is a talented man in the business world, shrewd, capable, enterprising, optimistic, fond of traveling, and fluent in twelve languages. He has been paying attention to the East for five years. In addition to three branch offices already established in Yokohama, Kobe, and other places in Japan, the company has also established a branch office at 467 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, in July of this year to purchase various Chinese manufactured products for sale in those countries. Because the company has many branch offices, sales are extremely convenient, so all goods are purchased in large quantities. Since the establishment of the branch office in Shanghai, it has become increasingly convenient to export Chinese manufactured products to the United States and Canadian markets. It is said that Mr. Jessberg's visit to Shanghai will not be delayed much. During his stay in Shanghai, he is very willing to have Chinese merchants and major manufacturers bring various samples of goods to the branch office on Jiangxi Road for negotiations, so that he can purchase as much as possible. It is also said that Mr. J. Rechter, the company's Far East purchasing agent, will accompany Mr. Jessberg. Mr. Rechter is the representative stationed in Shanghai and is well known to manufacturers in Shanghai and other ports.

City Taxi Drivers Demand Improved Treatment

The taxi driver workers in the city, in view of the harsh treatment and the fact that their monthly wages are all below thirty yuan, resulting in insufficient income to maintain daily life, the Shanghai Automobile Driver's Professional Union held an emergency meeting and decided to demand improved treatment. The working hours must not exceed twelve hours per day. The tip should be one yuan per car, and the gas tip should be two jiao, to be determined by the company. The union submitted the request to the trade association for negotiation, but it was ineffective. It has now formally presented it to the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Department, requesting a swift mediation. As for the Yunfei workers, they have requested that their wages be increased to forty yuan per month.

Shanghai Municipal Council Bus Employees' Demand; Social Affairs Bureau Mediation Ineffective

Shanghai Municipal Council Bus Company employees demanded double pay at the end of the year (that is, an annual bonus). After some employees went on strike and refused to sell tickets, fortunately, the Party and government authorities persuaded them to return to their original state. The Social Affairs Bureau yesterday afternoon at 2 pm convened labor and management for mediation. Mao Xinhui, the executive director of the Sixth District Bus Industry Professional Union, Liu Shouchun, the director, Huang Zhongwen, the general manager of the Shanghai Municipal Council Bus Company, Shi Ti, the head of the Transportation Department, and the social affairs coordinator of the Social Affairs Bureau were present. As the mediator, Zai Zhusun, was on leave, Zhu Quantao acted as chairman, and Jiang Shifu recorded the minutes. First, the management representative stated that the company's business has been repeatedly affected by the current situation, resulting in losses, and it is really impossible to bear the employee's annual bonus of one month's salary. He had explained the company's difficulties to the union director, but had not been understood. On the morning of the 23rd, the ticket sellers on each bus route went on strike and refused to sell tickets, causing unexpected losses to the company. It should be severely punished. Then, the labor representative stated that the employees' year-end bonus has been distributed every year, such as one month last year and twenty-three last year. This year, the company suddenly refused to issue it, and negotiations were ineffective, resulting in a strike. Fortunately, after trying their best to persuade them, they immediately returned to work. After the chairman's repeated persuasion, the management was still willing to issue a ten-day annual bonus, but it must be paid next year. The labor side conceded the annual bonus to twenty days, which must be issued this year, resulting in ineffective mediation. It was announced that the director would be consulted before proceeding with the review. The meeting adjourned at around 4 pm.

China Match Factory All Workers Strike

The China Match Factory in Pingjiangqiao, Zhabei, this city, has a total of more than five hundred male and female workers. Recently, a labor dispute arose because the workers demanded meal money during the shutdown period. After the Federation of Trade Unions sent someone to mediate, the factory agreed to pay each male worker one yuan and six jiao, but refused to pay the female workers. The workers were still dissatisfied. At 10 a.m. the day before yesterday, Wu Alian, a female worker in the factory's box department, was found by Shen Jingren, an employee of the factory, to have used the paste prepared in the factory, and was immediately notified to be suspended for a week. Wu expressed her dissatisfaction because she used very little paste and argued with the factory, requesting that the order be revoked. Later, the factory changed the fine to three boxes of matches for Wu's salary (120 boxes per box, totaling only four and a half cents in national currency). Wu was still dissatisfied, and the workers were usually dissatisfied with Shen's abuse of workers, so they believed that Shen was causing trouble, so they joined forces to help. All five hundred workers in the factory suddenly went on strike, demanding that the factory cancel Wu Alian's fine and replace Shen Jingren. Because the factory director, Pan Guiru, had gone to other ports to promote sales and no one was responsible, there was no result. The workers continued to strike yesterday and, at 10 a.m., sent representatives Tao Shubao and Wu Xiaolan to the Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Party Department, and the Federation of Trade Unions to petition, demanding that the factory be ordered to accept the conditions this time, and requesting that the decision to resolve the meal money for male and female workers during the shutdown period be resolved uniformly. After the Party and government agencies were petitioned, they all persuaded the workers to resume work first and wait for legal mediation.

Chen Yongji Injured by Car

Chen Yongji, a native of Ningbo, is 45 years old and lives at 14 Singapore Road, West Shanghai, renting a room. He works as a peddler. At about 9:30 last night, he was buying olives along the way when he passed the intersection of Gordon Road. A business car of the Republic Motor Company, number 18254, was traveling from west to east. Chen could not avoid it in time and was knocked to the ground, injuring his right eye. His injuries were serious. He was rushed to Baolong Hospital for treatment by the Chinese police officer number 360.

Perpetrator of Acid Attack, Shen Xisheng, Arrested

Zhang Yuanyan, who lives at 26 Sanxin Lane, Ailage Road, North Chujia Bridge, French Concession, was walking along Zhengjia Muqiao Street in the French Concession on August 5th of this year when he was suddenly splashed with nitric acid, causing severe facial injuries. The perpetrator fled the scene and Zhang reported it to the French police station and was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. It has been over four months and he has not yet recovered. The police station ordered the arrest of the perpetrator. It was discovered the day before yesterday by Detective Xiang that the perpetrator was Shen Xijin (age 27), a local resident living at 94 Vermon Road. He was arrested at that address and sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court yesterday. Judge Chen Shuoying questioned him. Chen Ming, the lawyer from the Police Department, stated that the victim is still in the hospital for treatment and that the reason for the perpetrator's actions needs to be investigated in detail. He requested a postponement. After verifying the confession in court, the defendant Shen Xisheng was questioned. He denied splashing acid. The court ordered that the hearing be rescheduled for the 29th. The defendant was remanded in custody, and a forensic doctor will be sent to Guangci Hospital to examine the victim's injuries for further verification.

Two Peddlers Commit Suicide Together; One Dies, One Survives

Zhou Xianbo (age 44), a local, and Shen Meisheng (age 37) were both peddlers. For unknown reasons, the two men decided to commit suicide together. On the afternoon of the 23rd, they purchased raw opium and went to the Huashang Inn at 140 Mofang Street, French Concession, and opened room number one, ostensibly to stay overnight. They divided the opium and ate it to commit suicide. After taking it, the two slept together in one bed, waiting for death to come. At 10 a.m. yesterday, Wang Qingfu, a waiter from Ningbo, went upstairs to urge the lodgers to get up and heard vomiting and moaning from room number one. He entered the room and found that Zhou had died in bed. Shen was vomiting and moaning incessantly. There were six small boxes of opium (two jiao each) on the table in front of the bed. Knowing that they had taken poison, he immediately reported it to the French police station, who sent detectives to investigate. Shen was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment, and Zhou's body was sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Parlor for an autopsy. No family members were found. A request was made today to the Second Special District Court to send someone to conduct an autopsy. Shen is expected to recover after treatment, but the reason why the two men committed suicide together is unknown and will be clarified after Shen is discharged from the hospital and questioned.

Photographic Society Sponsors National Photography Competition

The Chinese Photographic Society has been established for fifteen years, and has thousands of members at home and abroad. Chinese photography has long been backward, but thanks to the Society's vigorous promotion, great achievements have been made over the past ten years, which is unanimously praised by those engaged in photography. Moreover, the Society has repeatedly sponsored national photography annual and seasonal competitions to encourage photography, and has achieved good results. It is reported that as the Society marks its fifteenth anniversary, the Society has prepared valuable prizes such as silver shields, silver cups, and medals to sponsor the "10th National Photography Competition Conference" to promote photography. It is said that there are no fees for joining and that there are no restrictions on gender or level. All works by those who love photography (which must be enlarged from ten inches to eighteen inches) can participate in the competition. Detailed rules of war can be found in the Society's affiliated publication, "Photography News," issues 43 and 44 (one jiao including postage). The Society's address is currently at 138 Nanjing Road, Shanghai.

Shanghai Municipal Statistics Second Supplementary Materials Published; Compiled by the Shanghai Local Association

The Shanghai Local Association, in 1933, gathered dozens of experts to compile and publish "Shanghai Municipal Statistics" and in 1934 continued to compile the "Shanghai Municipal Statistics First Supplementary Materials." The two books were rich in material and accurate in numbers, and were praised by all sectors of politics, business, industry, and academia as indispensable tools for academic research. Subsequently, the Association, recognizing that statistical materials become more valuable over time, felt it necessary to continue compiling them. Therefore, it spared no expense and started compiling the Second Supplementary Materials this year, which were published on the 20th of this month after ten months. The content and compilation are richer and newer than before. The whole book has 159 pages and 250 tables, divided into (1) Land, (2) Population, (3) Justice, (4) Finance, (5) Finance, (6) Commerce, (7) Industry, (8) Labor, (9) Transportation, (10) Public Utilities, (11) Cultural Undertakings, (12) Education, (13) Society, (14) Health. To be seen as preferential treatment to readers, the price is one yuan per copy. Those interested in studying the economic and social problems of changing industries can purchase it at the Association at 415 Zhonghui Building, 415 Aiduya Road. All Shanghai Commercial Press, Shen Bao Hall, Authors' Publishing House, etc. are also sales agents.

Bai Yushuang's New Production of "The Amorous Empress"

Bai Yushuang, a famous female Dan performer of Bangbang Opera, has been performing at the Enpire Theatre in Baxianqiao since being hired last autumn, and has been praised by the people of Shanghai for over a year. After the premiere of new plays such as "Pan Jinlian" and "Romance of the Western Chamber" last month, the historical drama of the late Ming Dynasty "The Amorous Empress," which is rich in national consciousness, has been actively rehearsed and has been completed. The entire play is in Manchu costumes, all newly made, at an enormous cost. The expressions, singing, and acting of the hundreds of actors are extremely heavy. It took over three hours to complete the entire play. It will begin showing tonight (the 25th). Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather in Shandong and the Yellow River basin is clear and cold with northwesterly winds. The Yangtze River basin is cloudy, gradually becoming colder and drier, with northwesterly to northerly winds. The East Sea and Taiwan Bay are cloudy with rain, with strong winter winds. A small low-pressure system will pass over the Ryukyu Islands and move northeast-east, while a large low-pressure system or hurricane over or near the Yaps Islands is moving northwest. Also, the temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 2 PM yesterday reached a maximum of 40.6 and a minimum of 31.1. The same day last year saw a maximum of 40.5 and a minimum of 29.7.

Weather forecast for the week of Christmas: Cloudy, gradually clearing, still fine, colder, light fog in the morning, winds varying from northwest to northeast.

Electrical Manufacturing Industry in Shanghai (Continued)

— Edited by China Credit Bureau

(General Overview of Shanghai Industry and Commerce, No. 40)

8. Huade Light Bulb Factory—This factory was established in the 19th year of the Republic (1930) as a partnership by Tang Zixiang, Li Qingxiang, Li Qinghua, Cai Jünchen, Li Yüchi, and others, with a capital of 50,000 yuan. The enterprise is now valued at 300,000 yuan. It manufactures various types of light bulbs, and its annual turnover can reach 400,000 yuan. The factory address and general distribution center are located at 196 Ouyang Road, Zhabei. Distribution centers are located at 9 Jianghan Second Road, Hankou. The current manager is Mr. Tang Zixiang, and the assistant manager is Li Qinghua. The manager also serves as the chief engineer, Li Qingxiang. The factory owns its land, covering approximately 2.7 mu, valued at over 18,000 yuan. The factory buildings and workshops are valued at over 30,000 yuan, and the machinery and equipment are worth 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. Currently, the factory specializes in producing light bulbs, with a daily output of approximately 6,000 bulbs of various types.

9. Huiming Flashlight Battery Factory—This factory initially (in the 14th year of the Republic, 1925) only manufactured batteries, with a capital of only 3,000 yuan. Later, with the development of the business, it also manufactured flashlights, and the capital increased to 50,000 yuan. It is a sole proprietorship. The head of the battery department is Mr. Wang Song. The head of the flashlight department is Mr. Chen Qiyuan. Ding Nengzhao is the manager of the factory. The factory is located at 585-591 Qu Zhenren Road, Nanshi, and the distribution center is located at 9, Lane 427, Avenue Foch. The factory site is approximately four mu, half owned and half leased. The land and factory building renovations are worth over 25,000 yuan, and the machinery is worth 15,000 yuan. The products are trademarked with the "Da Wu Wei" (Fearless) brand.

10. Yaohua Flashlight General Factory—This factory was established ten years ago. It is a sole proprietorship operated by Mr. Zhang Chengxi, with a capital of approximately 40,000 to 50,000 yuan. It was initially located in Zhabei but was destroyed in the "January 28th" Incident and was moved to 50 Chenxiangge Road in the city. In addition to flashlights, it also manufactures batteries, electric essences, and light bulbs. The daily output of flashlights is approximately 120 to 130 dozen. The premises are leased, and the annual expenses, including employee salaries, amount to approximately 70,000 yuan.

11. China Storage Battery Factory—This factory was founded by Mr. Hu Guoguang as a sole proprietorship with a capital of 10,000 yuan in the 9th year of the Republic (1920). It manufactures various dry batteries and storage batteries. Because of their excellent quality, they are often purchased by the telegraph bureau. The annual turnover is approximately 100,000 yuan. The factory is located at the end of North Zhengxing Road, Zhabei, and a distribution center is located at 1, Lane 3, Yuqing Lane, Datong Road. The factory site is approximately three mu, with 30 self-owned rooms (bungalows). The main machinery includes a spraying machine, a punching machine, and three motors, with 240 employees.

Indian Attar Challenges Huang Bochang Again; Match Scheduled for Next Tuesday

Huang Bochang, our country's famous American-style wrestling master, has shaken China and the world with his fame after defeating Indian strongmen Mihara and Pihavan twice. Lin Zecang Invents Family Table Tennis Game

Lin Zecang, the initiator of the Shanghai Table Tennis Federation and chairman of the All-China Table Tennis Federation, has recently invented "Family Table Tennis Game," which is most suitable for Chinese and Japanese families. After its implementation, ordinary households can purchase it. It can replace bad habits such as smoking, drinking, prostitution, and gambling, and it is also a very popular fitness exercise. Regardless of age or gender, it requires very little space, is easy and economical to set up, and can be held anytime, anywhere. Its nature is peaceful and stimulating. The competition is very interesting and not intense.

General Overview of Education in Jiangxi Province in the 24th Year of the Republic

The following is a summary of the general overview of education in Jiangxi Province in the 24th year of the Republic, based on the results of the survey. The province's educational expenses for the 24th year of the Republic were 2,100,002 yuan, distributed as follows: Agricultural College 15 yuan, accounting for 37.14 percent (hereinafter, the word "percent" is omitted); Specialized Schools 1,658,307 yuan, accounting for 7.89; Middle Schools 408,234 yuan, accounting for 19.42; Vocational Schools 218,292 yuan, accounting for 10.18; Normal Schools 309,645 yuan, accounting for 4.73; Studying Abroad 18,290 yuan, accounting for 5.63; Social Education 123,562 yuan, accounting for 5.88; Provincial Elementary Schools 372,506 yuan, accounting for 17.72; Subsidies, Stipends, and Awards 100,000 yuan, accounting for 4.76; Affiliated Institutions 10,032 yuan, accounting for 0.48; Educational Miscellaneous Expenses 46,852 yuan, accounting for 2.23; and Institutional Construction 78,757 yuan, accounting for 3.74. The county educational expenses for the 24th year of the Republic were 1,041,890 yuan.

Regarding compulsory education in elementary education, there were 5,900 schools, 244,645 students, and 2,022,704 yuan in expenses in the 22nd year of the Republic. In the latter half of the 23rd year of the Republic, the number of schools increased by 2,776, the number of students increased by 139,940, and the expenses increased by 656,731 yuan. In the first half of the 24th year of the Republic, the number of schools increased by 10,192, the number of students increased by 498,575, and the expenses for supporting education increased by 1,580,604 yuan. Compared with the figures for the 22nd year of the Republic, both the number of schools and the number of students have more than doubled. It is estimated that there are more than 25,000 schools throughout the province, and 4,000 new schools are established each year. It is hoped that compulsory education will be universal in the province after five years. There are 37 elementary schools with 236 classes and 11,376 students in the provincial capital. In addition, there are 13 schools affiliated with the Provincial Normal School and the Provincial Central Elementary School, with 102 classes and 4,607 students.

Regarding secondary education, there are 35 public and private middle schools with 9,587 students, 14 normal schools with 2,175 students, and 15 vocational schools with 1,661 students. The province's policy for secondary education is to limit the establishment of new schools and, depending on local needs, convert them into vocational or rural normal schools. On the one hand, the content of existing middle schools is improved, and on the other hand, vocational and normal education facilities are expanded as much as possible. Therefore, the number of middle schools has been decreasing since the 21st year of the Republic, and vocational and normal schools have been built to fill the void.

Regarding higher education, there are specialized schools, including the provincial agricultural, medical, and technological schools. In the 23rd year of the Republic, the agricultural school was transferred to the provincial agricultural college. In the 24th year of the Republic, there were 281 students in the two specialized schools. As for studying abroad, there was one student studying engineering in the United States and one student studying medicine.

Regarding various social education endeavors, in addition to establishing a music education committee, expanding the provincial sports field, enriching the provincial science museum, and reorganizing the provincial library and civic education center, efforts have been made to promote civic education, including organizing itinerant education film groups, promoting radio education, vigorously carrying out popular lectures, unifying the training of people's work, compiling people's reading materials, establishing itinerant people's schools, and short-term elementary schools in the provincial capital. Furthermore, progress has been made in scouting training and the promotion of music education, health education, the implementation of civic training in the provincial capital, the promotion of simplified education in the provincial capital, and the organization of youth new life labor service groups.

Students from Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui Ethnic Groups Petition for Subsidies for Further Education

Deadline is limited to the end of January next year for submission.

The Ministry of Education specifically ordered universities to inform accordingly.

The Ministry of Education recently issued an order to all public and private specialized schools and universities in the country, stating that in order to encourage students from the Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui ethnic groups to pursue further education in specialized schools and universities in the mainland and to seek advanced studies, the ministry promulgated the "Outline of Measures for Subsidizing Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui Students to Pursue Further Education in Specialized Schools and Universities in the Mainland" on November 23 of this year, and ordered that they be informed accordingly. Recently, many Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students have complied with the aforementioned regulations and petitioned for subsidies. Fearing that there may be Mongolian, Tibetan, and Hui students in various specialized schools and universities who are unaware of these regulations, resulting in omissions, all are limited to preparing the various procedures in accordance with the provisions of Article 4 of the aforementioned Outline of Measures and submitting them to the Ministry by the end of January of the 26th year of the Republic for review and approval. No further petitions will be accepted after the deadline. In addition to issuing separate instructions, the Ministry hereby orders that all schools immediately publicize this information. This order.

Measures for Students from Northeast China to Pursue Further Education and Transfer Schools

In order to provide guidance for students from Northeast China to pursue further education and transfer schools, the Ministry of Education recently issued a special order to all public and private universities in the country, stating that the Northeast Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry of Education had submitted the "Measures for Students from Northeast China to Pursue Further Education and Transfer Schools" for review and implementation. After review, these measures were found to be feasible. In addition to issuing instructions and separate instructions, the Ministry hereby issues these measures to all schools for information. This order.

Preparation for the Alumni Association of the National Research Institute

Previously, universities in China established various research institutes one after another in order to pursue advanced academic research. However, the administrative system has always belonged to the university headquarters, and there has been a lack of organizational connections between the various research institutes. Since the Ministry of Education promulgated the Research Institute Organization Law two years ago, research institutes have reached an independent status and are the highest stage in the academic system. More than 30 research institutes have been registered with the Ministry of Education. In order to promote academic cooperation and emotional connections between the various institutes, the Alumni Association of the National Sun Yat-sen University Research Institute plans to initiate a National Research Institute Alumni Association. It is reported that it has already begun to investigate the situation of new and old alumni in various research institutes across the country, as well as their opinions on the organization of the association. Once the investigation is completed, it plans to start the process immediately.

Municipal Education Association Launches Campaign to Reduce Textbook Prices

In recent years, the price of textbooks has been increasing day by day, and the students' burden is too heavy, which is enough to affect the popularization of education. In view of this, the Shanghai Municipal Education Association has decided to launch a campaign to reduce the price of textbooks in order to reduce the burden on students. In addition to submitting a petition to the Social Bureau to forward it to the Ministry of Education, instructing all bookstores to uniformly reduce prices, it has also been distributed to the education associations of various provinces and cities to jointly report. At the same time, it has been decided to convene all primary and secondary school principals in the city within days to strive for the achievement of the goal.

Inspection of Overseas Chinese Education: Commissioner Fang Wei Returns to Shanghai

Mr. Fang Wei, a special commissioner dispatched by the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission to investigate overseas Chinese education, has returned to the country. Yesterday, he discussed his experiences during the inspection of overseas Chinese education as follows: "I was ordered to inspect overseas Chinese education in Nanyang. On July 28th, I departed from Nanjing to Shanghai. On August 12th, I boarded the British ship 'Empress of Japan'. On the 14th, I passed through Hong Kong. On the 16th, I arrived in Manila. On the 24th, I took a train to San Taloc, and returned to Manila the same day. On September 1st, I left Manila, arrived in Iloilo the next day, in Cebu on the 3rd, in Zamboanga on the 5th, in Cotabato on the 13th, and in Sulu on the 15th, which is the southernmost part of the American Philippine Islands. On the 17th, I arrived in Sandakan in British North Borneo. On the 22nd, I arrived in Kudat, on the 23rd in Jesselton, on the 24th in Labuan, on the 25th in Miri, passed through Kuching on the 26th, and arrived in Singapore on the 28th. On October 6th, I went to Johor, returning to Singapore the same day. On the 22nd, I took a ship to Burma. On the 24th, I passed through Penang. On the 28th, I arrived in Rangoon, Burma. On November 2nd, I left Rangoon, and on the 4th, I returned to Penang. On the 9th, I entered the Malay States, passed through Taiping to Ipoh, arrived in Kuala Lumpur on the 12th, in Malacca on the 15th, and returned to Singapore on the 17th. On the 20th, I boarded the postal ship 'President Doumergue'. On the 23rd, I arrived in Xizhi, French Annam. On the 28th, I took a train from Saigon, and arrived in Hanoi on the 30th. On December 2nd, I arrived in Haiphong. On the 4th, I took a ship from Haiphong, arrived in Beihai on the 5th, in Haikou on the 6th, in Hong Kong on the 8th, went to Guangzhou on the 11th, and returned to Hong Kong on the 12th. I returned yesterday via Xiamen. I will return to Nanjing immediately to report my mission. This trip lasted 153 days, passing through territories of England, France, and America, visiting a total of 28 ports, inspecting 162 schools, participating in 42 lectures at overseas Chinese organizations and schools, and 72 tea parties, banquets, and discussions. I have obtained a considerable amount of information and opinions on overseas Chinese schools. After returning to Nanjing, I will organize a detailed report to be submitted to the Ministry of Education and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for review."
