Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk Market Strong; Factory Merchants and Silk Merchants Hold Prices More Firmly

This week, the overseas silk market has gradually rebounded, and it was even stronger yesterday. New York's Japanese silk was at 83.75 cents, and Shanghai silk was at 78 cents, both up 5 cents. Guangdong silk was up 4 cents. The exchange's near-term contracts were up 2 cents, and far-term contracts were up 3 cents. Jicang spot prices were up 15 yuan, and futures prices were up 24 yuan. The market atmosphere was instantly prosperous. Only Lyons silk prices remained stubbornly unchanged. In the local silk market, firms such as Jardine had sales yesterday, but because Christmas was near, and domestic silk merchants held prices more firmly, sales were not very smooth. Sales by factories included White Factory with a uniformity of 85 at 900 yuan, a uniformity of 78 for coarse silk at 755 yuan, and Jin Ai Ying grade at 785 yuan, all of which were considered firm prices. Total sales, both domestic and foreign, were 120 bales. Western merchants are closed today, and there will also be no market on the 26th. The silk market will depend on the situation in the next adjustment.

The Downward Trend in Piece Goods and Cotton Cloth Has Gradually Subsided; Japanese Factories Refuse to Open Forward Contracts

The cloth market showed a slight turnaround yesterday, due to the sharp rise in the Osaka yarn and cloth market. Local Japanese yarn factories were also watching with interest, refusing to open forward contracts for brocade cloth. Retailers in the cloth industry, facing a glut of spot goods, were also eager to sell. However, some who held large quantities had changed their strategy and slightly held up prices. Therefore, the downward trend in yesterday's market had gradually subsided. However, differing opinions led to extreme chaos in the market, with prices 5 cents per piece higher than the previous session. A large number of cheap goods previously contracted by the Guanggang from the Bengchang fine twill were shipped from various Japanese factories. Because the market in Guangdong was not good, many were resold in Shanghai to other gangs, with dyeing factories absorbing more. Prices were down about 10 cents per piece. Coarse cloth, coarse twill, dyed goods, and printed goods prices were all stable. Actual sales remained slow. Only sporadic transactions were made along the various routes. The dispatch of confirmed orders was as busy as usual. With the end of the year approaching, factories were eager to close out confirmed orders. Yesterday, dyeing factories absorbed fine cloth and fine twill from the Huai Dong series, such as the Dragon Head and Five-Width Yang He brands, as well as fine twill from various Bengchang brands. The Shugang bought over 100 cases of undyed and gray fine twill, it is said.

Dried and Preserved Goods: New Qing Cakes Prices Turn Upward

The arrival of new Qing cakes has been scarce recently, and market sentiment has tightened. It was heard yesterday that Taier goods opened at 6.12 yuan, up 30 to 40 cents from before. Current sales in the inland areas of Water Street and the Wintai gang are still active. Higher quality goods are sold at 6.60 yuan to 6.73 yuan. Discounts may apply.

Rain

— Zhang Chunqiao

The rain is falling a little slower now, but the wind has picked up. The raindrops, panicked and uneasy, huddle against the windowpane, as if by doing so, the wind wouldn't be able to catch them. Though there aren't many raindrops, they make quite a noise.

I'm alone in my room, writing this letter to you with a sense of loneliness, no, almost a pang of sadness.

Sitting here in my chair, holding my pen, I don't know what to tell you first.

The window faces north, and it's always dark here. No sunlight penetrates the gloom, and a damp smell wafts from the corners of the room, making the air so heavy it feels like it can't circulate. I don't dare stay here too long. I'm always running around, hoping to bask in the sun a little more. I'd love to go to the nearby park, sit on the grass, and read a book. That would be so wonderful for my weak body. But, as you know, those books have educated us, and they don't allow someone like you or me to rest for even a moment, all for the sake of the sunshine that will forever illuminate our future.

These past few days, I really haven't been able to keep it up. My legs can't carry me very far before they feel like they're being dragged by someone. Add to that the hardships life has thrown my way. They advised me to rest for a bit, and during these few days of leisure, write something to earn some money to sustain me next month. I haven't been able to do it. I don't want to write anything frivolous, but meaningful works can't be published. So I've been spending all my time reading books I usually don't have time to read.

But the news in the papers has been disturbing me, making it impossible to concentrate.

Tonight, the rain started to fall. It's deathly dark in this room. It's as if all the light in the world has vanished. The thick, damp smell crowds around me, as if trying to suffocate me.

I want to go outside. My leather shoes are long since broken. How can I withstand the icy water and mud that seep into my shoes from the asphalt and dirt roads on a cold day like this? Besides, where would I go?

Just then, the rain began to howl wildly again, mixing with the wind and violently assaulting the earth. It's rare to encounter rain like this in early winter. It's as if it wants to destroy the world, no, to wash away all the filth, even the depression in my heart.

I am surrounded by a magnificent symphony.

I can't hear any other sounds.

My entire attention is captured by the storm.

I don't know when the door opened.

"Mr. Peng!"

The person calling me was a blurry figure. Her voice was raised, as if she had run a long way, and her throat was blocked by something, making her voice a little hoarse and trembling. It sounded familiar, yet I couldn't remember whose voice it was.

I flipped the light switch.

It was Sha?

She was wearing her old, dark blue gown, which had turned black from the rain. Water droplets sparkled as they slid down her face, and her hair was plastered to her head. A heavy strand hung limply on her cheek, beside her left ear. Her eyes, shining with a fire-like heat, stared at me, and when I looked at her in astonishment, she smiled!

"The rain is so heavy, you..."

"Is it strange?"

As she spoke, she took off her coat. I took my own worn-out cotton gown from my trunk to give to her, but she waved it away. She lay down on my bed, pulled the quilt over herself.

I pulled the chair closer to her.

She lay on her side, her hands on the quilt, her face exposed, her wet hair spread across the pillow. She looked very tired, resting.

I was surprised that she knew I lived here, and that she had run out in such a storm, wearing such thin clothes.

I had met her at a school. During the first class, I realised she was a talented person. Her abundant talent was still a virgin land, just waiting to be cultivated. Her academic results were astonishing. I simply couldn't believe that she had never studied before, or that she hadn't known how to speak Mandarin. In a very short period, she was already able to write fluent, excellent essays and speak accurate Mandarin.

But that was four months ago. I hadn't seen her since she graduated from the school. I had only heard from others that she was teaching, and doing very well. I had also heard that she wanted to talk to me to resolve some questions she had.

But we had never met.

How could I not be surprised by her sudden arrival today?

I looked at her. Her eyes were fixed on the ceiling, silent, as if she were recalling a story or a romantic dream.

"Where did you come from?"

"I was just about to tell you." She paused for a moment. "Haven't you seen the news in the papers? Things are very tense outside!"

Excitement shone on her face. She seemed to be forcing her voice down, but it was still very loud. The howling of the wind and rain poured in from outside, as if trying to drown it out.

"Could you close the window? The wind is too strong..."

"Of course, tell me,"

I turned and closed the window, and the room became quiet. All that could be heard was the howling of the wind and rain outside.

I looked at her excited face, remaining silent.

"How did you think to come here?"

"I had nowhere else to go, then I remembered you."

"Because you're our teacher! We often talk about you, and we often think of you when something happens. We always hope to get your opinion. These days, you haven't been coming, and we think of you even more often—but, are you feeling better?"

Her tone was steady and clear. Her innocent eyes smiled. She only fell silent after I nodded at her reassuringly.

I looked out the window. The lamplight shone out, clearly dividing the raindrops, like countless cotton threads, shredded by the wind, falling to the ground, disappearing.

I still didn't have a cotton coat, or any preparations for winter. But her enthusiasm, my anxieties were all melted by that heat. My health seemed to have been restored as well.

Tomorrow, I'll get back to everything.

晨

— Gao Erji (Gorky) 作, Ren Jun 譯

The most interesting thing in the world is to see how a day is born.

The first light of the sun shines brightly in the sky, the darkness of night quietly hiding into the valleys and cracks in the rocks, hiding in the leaves of the trees and covered with morning dew, just like in the lace-knitting grass. At this time, the tops of the mountains smile kindly, as if saying to the gentle night shadows: "Don't be afraid—this is the sun!"

The waves of the sea raise their white heads, like the beautiful women of the court, bowing to the sun as if to their king, singing:

"Master of the world, we joyfully welcome you!"

The kind sun smiles. These waves have been playing and rolling all night; now their hair is disheveled, their green clothes are wrinkled, and the velvet skirts are tangled.

"Good day!" says the sun, rising above the sea. "Good day, beautiful gentlemen! But—enough is enough, give me some peace! If you continue to jump so high, won't the children be unable to bathe? Shouldn't we make everything on earth comfortable?"

Green lizards jump out of the cracks in the rocks, blinking their sleepy eyes, talking to each other.

"It will be hot today!"

On hot days, flies will fly around in depression, and it will be easy for lizards to catch them to eat. Devouring delicious flies is—the most delightful thing! It turns out that lizards are—very particular about what they eat and drink!

Flowers, wet with dew, sway each other in a playful manner, as if teasingly saying:

"Sir, please describe how beautiful we are when we are decorated with dewdrops in the early morning! Please look at us and describe the little portraits of various flowers in words, please try it! It's a very easy thing—we are such simple things..."

These little mischievous devils! They know perfectly well that people cannot describe their adorable beauty in words—they are laughing!

I respectfully take off my hat and say to the flowers: "Your sincerity is truly undeserved. Thank you for your kindness—but I don't have time at the moment, maybe later..."

When the flowers stretch their hands and feet towards the sun, as if proudly smiling, the sun's rays shine on the dewdrops, carving diamond-like brilliance on the petals and green leaves.

In the meantime, on the flowers, there is already a large group, a large group of yellow bees, as if greedily sucking on sweet honey. Moreover, their low and rough singing is still flowing in the warm air:

Celebrating the sun, the source of happy life,

Celebrating the merit of beautifying the earth.

The red-breasted robin has woken up. Standing on its slender feet, swaying its body, it also sings its own quiet, joyful song. — Birds know better than people how realistic it is to live on earth. Robins are always the first to greet the sun. And because the feathers on this little bird's small chest are still dyed by the morning light, in distant and cold Russia, this bird is even called "Morning Star." In the bushes, that cheerful, gray-green bird is jumping around. This bird is very much like the children on the street—extremely irritable, and never tired no matter how much you call.

Swallows fly as lightly as black arrows, chasing small insects, calling out happily, blissfully—having light wings is delightful.

The branches of the umbrella pine are trembling—the umbrella pine is like a large wine glass; the sunlight is like golden wine overflowing.

At this moment, people have also woken up. Their entire lives are—hard work; their lives are all about decorating and enriching this earth—but, from birth to death, they themselves remain poor.

Why?

If you want to know the reason, you will understand when you grow up. For now—just love the sun, the source of all joy and strength. And, just as the sun treats everyone equally, try to be kind and cheerful as much as possible.

People have woken up. Then they go out to farm, go out to work—the sun looks at them and smiles. Humankind has done so many good things on earth: it knows better than anyone else. The sun has witnessed that the earth was once a desert; now, the earth has been completely covered by the great work of humankind—our fathers, grandfathers, and great-grandfathers, by important things that children cannot understand. They have also created various toys and various pleasant things on earth—among them, especially things like movies.

Ah, our ancestors, they worked hard. Therefore, we should cherish and respect the great work they have done that is everywhere around us.

Young people, you might as well try to think about this matter—narrating the chapters of how humankind works on earth is—the most interesting story in the world...

On the wild fence, roses are scarlet, and her flowers are blooming everywhere, while ordinary flowers have withered; but they are still gazing at the blue sky, gazing at the golden sun. The velvety petals, swaying, emit a sweet fragrance, in the fragrant, green, warm atmosphere, gently drifting soft songs:

Even if withered

Beautiful is still—beautiful

Even if dead

Lovely is still—lovely...

Another day has arrived.

Good day, young people! May you have many good days in your life!

As I write this, I feel lonely.

The child of the past is now forty years old, but has not done any work.—He feels a bit lonely.

Thoughts on My Fourth Sister's Marriage

— Chen Yi

Yesterday, I received a letter from my father saying that my fourth sister will get married on the third day of the tenth month. After reading this news, besides sighing that as a son, I cannot share a little of my old father's burden, I sat quietly for a while before exhaling a breath.

"Fourth sister! Another victim."

Fourth sister also has dizzy spells. When a dizzy spell comes on, she doesn't know anything. However, because my father is constantly running around outside to support the family, and my mother has a weak body, and the two older sisters have already married out, and the younger sister is an ignorant seven-year-old child, all the affairs of the family fall on fourth sister's shoulders. She manages the oil, salt, firewood, and rice, she manages the family's laundry, and also manages receiving guests. When I went home last year, I had to ask her for a thread. My mother often said that my younger sister is young, and I haven't taken a wife yet. What will happen when fourth sister gets married one day? So fourth sister's in-laws have come several times to ask for her birth date, but my mother has insisted on not giving it, for this very reason.

But as the country people often say, "Girls are outsiders." Daughters will eventually marry when they grow up. After reading my father's letter, I should be happy, I should congratulate my sister, but I am indeed extremely uneasy. I thought of my two married sisters.

In our hometown, such a remote mountainous area, regarded by others as an uncivilized place, it is common for daughters to be uneducated. My family is not a special class, so my sisters certainly didn't go to school. They themselves didn't have the freedom to choose their own marriages, and their parents were limited by the era they lived in, so they could do nothing about arranging their children's marriages. Although this arrangement was done with careful selection, because it was an arrangement after all, the result would not be good.

The older sister married a farmer's son. The brother-in-law is said to have studied for a few days, but he is unwilling to improve himself, preferring to do something for the community. My sister is a very strong-willed person. Seeing that her brother could run to Beijing and Shanghai, she thought her husband could do the same. But assuming her husband really did that one day, and found a woman outside and abandoned her, this, she never thought of.

On the first night of her marriage, she was ravaged like an animal, unable to resist. Etiquette taught her that this was human relations and should be endured. Getting pregnant, having children, the in-laws were afraid of spending money on a wet nurse, so on the first day after giving birth, they squeezed her milk. According to physiological knowledge, milk comes on the third day for a new mother. Eventually, she squeezed out a milk sore, which didn't heal for half a year.

No one cared about her sore. She came home to get medical treatment. When I saw my mother pulling out the pus, a shadow immediately appeared before my eyes, and I couldn't help but shudder. I almost shouted.

My mother bent over, I held the lamp, my sister sat on the chair. When my mother's hand touched the sore, my sister screamed miserably. This miserable scream particularly struck my heart, like a needle pricking it. The country doctors were unbelievably ignorant. They put a bundle of grass of unknown name on the stove to bake, and didn't even apply it to the sore, saying it could cure the disease. Only heaven knew if this was true. Trying to buy some of the most common Western medicine was like looking for a needle in a haystack. Watching my sister get thinner day by day, and the sore never closing, my mother was so anxious that she couldn't eat.

But her husband acted as if nothing had happened. It wasn't until they asked someone to buy medicine in the city and treated her according to my own little medical knowledge that she slowly improved. But half of my sister's hair had fallen out, and she was so thin she was unrecognizable. The first letter I received from my father after leaving home was about my sister's affair.

"Ju Nu's illness has recovered, but the family has already separated, ×× has not studied, doesn't know anything, alas! Ju Nu is also a person with a hard life."

What else could I say?

The second sister married a high school graduate. Although her husband smoked opium, gambled, and frequented prostitutes, fortunately, he was still good to my sister, but there was a reason for this: because he had a stepmother.

The stepmother treated my sister harshly. No matter how humble my sister was, she could never please the stepmother. Apart from getting pregnant and having children like the older sister, this sister was a bit healthier and more honest, so she could still get by. But every day, from the moment she got up in the morning, she cooked, fed the pigs, washed clothes, until she went to sleep, she could rest.

When I left home, my sister was living like this, and she wasn't even allowed to come to her in-law's house to see me off. In the next ten years, twenty years, until death, if society is still the same as it is today, my sister's situation probably won't change in the slightest.

Thinking of the experiences of these two sisters, I truly pity fourth sister, who will get married on the third day of the tenth month. As I read the letter, I thought to myself, although I have figured out the reason and deeply believe in it, I am sad.

Thinking of a remote countryside thousands of miles away, a house, a small room, a rough man embracing a pure woman, doing what is called human relations, my eyes turned black, and shadows appeared before my eyes, one, two, three...

Farewell

— TK

Dusk at Lian Lake

— Qian Dong

Alone by the white-walled inn on my journey,

The scenery of the fading year hastens homesickness,

In the cold night, no one speaks,

The bright moon fills the boat, the sound of wild geese.

Good mountains beyond the clouds seem to have an appointment,

Wild trees in the mist are of unknown name.

Tomorrow at the Magpie Bridge, it will be lively,

It must be that families are coming out to welcome their kin.

——Sa Dula: Passing Lian Lake at the End of the Year

The impression my hometown gave me was originally very faint; especially in recent years, no matter where I went to make a living, I always dragged a long tail behind me: my mother, sister, wife, children, my hometown followed me, I never worried about not hearing the harsh local accent of my hometown, I could always see the messy belongings of my family, my hometown and I had no more ties.

This year, my hometown suddenly moved to Danyang.

Danyang is a place praised by poets and writers of the past. Next to this ancient canal is the Jade Milk Spring of Danyang Guanyin Temple, which was rated as the fourth spring in the world by Zhang Youxin of the Tang Dynasty. There, poets often sang: "Fetching jade milk spring water is worth boiling, sitting in the moonlight talking about emptiness, wanting to be with the monks." And Lian Lake, opposite the Jade Milk Spring, is even more what they yearn for. "Faint light waves, gentle breeze," "Just when the moon is bright and the tea is ripe, listening to the lotus-picking song across the lake," these are all clear songs that sway from the poets' small boats on the lake.

This evening, after class, I wanted to shake off the fatigue on my body, so I went alone along the canal. The banks of the canal are no longer "rich in merchants" as Li Bai said, but everything seems to have declined. On the turbid river water, which is as muddy as mud, only a few old men are fishing; on the desolate embankments, which are covered with weeds, are scattered the grass sheds of Jiangbei people.

The north wind roared as if it wanted to swallow people, walking across the embankment, the wind seemed to blow even harder. Shrinking my body, I walked to the lakeside.

Darkness hung down like a curtain, the vast lake surface was like being covered with a layer of black veil, the gloomy waves surging, crashing against the lakeside. Looking at the sky, it was also covered with dark clouds, it was probably going to snow soon.

Of course, I don't have the elegance and fortune to come to this lakeside to taste tea; and I don't have the mood to listen to mountain songs across the lake. But I only hope to see the mirror-like water on the vast lake surface. However, darkness quickly hung down, and the surging waves still crashed.

In this broken era and at the edge of these broken years and days, at the edge of this vast dark sky and this vast dark Lian Lake, a person who never thinks of hometown now remembers that he needs a place like hometown.

Sa Dula, your boat passed by here, please tell me, where should I moor?

Gide's "New Fruits"

— Quan Lin

When Mephistopheles was about to tempt Faust, the Heavenly Emperor said to him:

"The branches and leaves are lush, even the gardener knows,

There will be a harvest of flowers and fruits next year."

But Faust never harvested his fruit after all. Mephistopheles won. Faust ended in tragedy.

Goethe, with great enthusiasm, pursued the resolution of real contradictions, pursued a complete personality, but after he finished writing Faust, he sighed to Eckerman: "It is beyond human power to solve the problems of the world; he can only find out where the problems begin, and stay within the limits of what he can understand. His function does not allow him to understand the activities of nature. It is futile for him to try to understand the universe with a limited perspective. The principles of man and God are two completely different things." As this great poet gradually aged, he finally felt tired.

Goethe's ennui was precisely the ennui of many great artists in the 19th century. With their great genius, they recognized the contradictions and ugliness of reality, but they could not find a way out to solve it. They wanted to find a fulfilling life, but they felt that they could not find it in this real world; so they hesitated, were distressed, and did not know what to do. Finally, they hid in the embrace of idealism or religion to seek comfort—this almost became a representative tone in 19th-century literature and art.

Now, looking at it from a historical perspective, we can understand why these great artists could not find their way out. It was not because their genius was not great enough, but because their historical era limited them. When they lived in a historical era based on individualism, and tried to find a way out for this era from an individualistic approach, as Goethe said, it was futile.

We should be grateful for being born in this era. We have seen not only in theory but also in practice a new future for humanity. The flowers of a new social system that have bloomed from the historical soil of individualism have answered the questions that the predecessors could not solve. A free, unoppressed society is in our prospect. From there we can find a complete personality, find humanity's true happiness. But this new era has not yet arrived—perhaps it is still quite a distance from us. This requires us to reach it with even more arduous and determined efforts. In such an arduous struggle process, we may encounter greater distress and disappointment. How will we overcome these distresses (which can be said to be the general distresses of modern youth)? Gide's "New Fruits" (Les Nouvelles Nouritures, published in 1935) gives us a clear answer.

With what attitude will we face this reality? The author tells us:

"Raise your lowered head. Raise your eyes that are looking down into the tomb, but don't raise them too high, to look at the vast sky, but look at the horizon. Comrade, boldly, renewedly, prepare to leave this place corrupted by the poisonous bacteria of corpses, and go where your steps guide you. Let your hope push you forward. Don't let yourself be pulled back by the love of the past! Move forward to the future. It is enough to seek poetry from your dreams; now you must learn to find it in reality. If it is not there, then create it yourself."

Yes, create it. Human beings are determined by reality, but at the same time they are also creating reality. How we will create a new reality cannot be solved in the circle of individualism. We need to have a new outlook on life:

"Know how to acquire that which makes lamentation useless! Do not beg from others what you cannot obtain yourself.

"...Build your happiness on the creation of happiness for all. Work, struggle, and do not accept things that you cannot change. You must learn to repeat this sentence: Everything depends on myself. It is cowardly for people to bow their heads to the evils caused by themselves. Don't think anymore—if you have ever thought this way—that submission is clever, otherwise, don't go to this kind of cleverness for inspiration again.

"Comrade, do not accept the life that others give you. Continue to pursue yourself, that which can improve life—this is our life, your life, and the life of all; not that kind of future life that people say can give us comfort in this present life, that calls us to endure misfortune. Do not accept it! When you know that it is man, not God, who should be responsible for all the evils in life, you will no longer succumb to evil.

"Do not make any more sacrifices to idols."

Building your happiness on the creation of happiness for all is the most important point. Your happiness and the happiness of all cannot be separated. People must satisfy themselves only when all can satisfy themselves. This does not depend on Faustian erudition, but on knowing "how to acquire that which makes lamentation useless"—struggle. It is people themselves, not God, who create all evils, and people should not succumb to all evils. People must have the courage to break the surface of this evil society in order to achieve their happiness. Believe in your own strength, and continue to struggle against all idols, all things that oppress humanity. Transform reality and create reality through struggle. Only at such a price can we achieve humanity's true happiness, can we obtain humanity's true liberation, can we create a complete personality, can humanity conquer nature, can we obtain the so-called "unlimited expansion of love."

Gide's "New Fruits" grows out of the soil of reality. It has not a trace of metaphysical odor (although this gardener was once a faithful Christian). It is a valuable treasure for young people.

Page 17

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Brief Notes

Using Chinese Learning as the Core and Western Learning for Application

— Hua

Chinese society is a very ancient, conservative, yet contradictory society. To prove that I am not talking nonsense, let's talk about doctors.

Chinese medicine is said to have been invented very early. Since Shennong tasted hundreds of herbs, for thousands of years, after the experience of many famous doctors, the theory of Yin-Yang and the Five Elements and various mysterious principles have also been invented, making it difficult for the general public to fathom its profundity. In the last century, due to the opening of the sea, the Chinese people have come to know that the so-called "world" also includes countries that are not barbarian tribes besides "Hua Xia". When Chinese people suffer from diseases and feel that Hua Tuo cannot be reborn, when they have no other way, they have to ask Western doctors for advice. In fact, it is because of this need that more and more people are learning Western medicine. Now, the business of Western medicine is gradually developing, and patients' belief in them has also increased due to facts.

In big cities, the situation of Chinese medicine and Western medicine being on opposite sides has turned into a situation of one pressing and one retreating. The retreating side even feels a bit unsustainable, so they realize the power of some kind of weapon of the other side and try to imitate it. But unfortunately, the doctor's responsibility is to save lives, not to kill. Using Western medicine methods to resist Western medicine will not only fail to resist, but will also often put patients at risk of dying in vain. I have encountered some patients who are bound by traditional concepts, believing that for certain diseases, Chinese medicine is not good, such as surgery, which must be taught by Western medicine, but for certain internal medicine symptoms, Chinese medicine is indispensable. They generally believe in the famous saying "Chinese learning as the core, Western learning for application," and for medicine, they also believe that only a combination of Chinese and Western medicine can cure the disease. Some patients often take Chinese medicine and get Western medicine injections, thinking that this combination of Chinese and Western medicine will cure the disease faster, but there are also times when both Chinese and Western medicine are helpless.

On the one hand, because patients have this need, and on the other hand, to show their intelligence, some Chinese medicine doctors also administer injections themselves, such as antipyretic injections and serum injections. Some Chinese medicine doctors even bring their own medicine, so Western doctors don't have to bother anymore. However, after the injection is given, whether there is a reaction in the patient, what the degree of the reaction is, and whether there is any damage to other parts of the body, is unknown. In this situation, patients can only rely on fate.

Recently, there was a report that a Chinese medicine doctor was "falsely using Western medicine and Western medical equipment, which was prohibited by the former Ministry of Health. The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, in view of the fact that a few Chinese medicine doctors still abuse Western medicine and syringes to treat people, specially ordered all Chinese medicine groups to strictly abide by the prohibition and send inspectors to investigate at any time to crack down on it and value people's lives...etc." If it were not for the threat to patients' lives, the Health Bureau would not have told them to "value people's lives." My bringing this up does not mean that I am opposed to Chinese medicine. Although Chinese medicine has thousands of years of history, due to the high-speed progress of the times, it cannot reverse its fate. Today, due to the development of transportation and the prevalence of machinery, some diseases unique to metropolises cannot only not be cured by Chinese medicine, but even the causes of the diseases cannot be known. Because such disease names do not exist in ancient medical books, they can only blindly guess the "symptoms." To give an example, the causes of "cancer" have not been found by "cancer" experts in Europe, America, and Japan, so Western doctors are helpless when they encounter cancer. However, our Chinese medicine doctors are said to have a way to cure this problem, but Mr. Huang Yingbai ultimately died.

These words are all facts, without any emotionality or contempt for Chinese medicine. I believe that at this time, Chinese medicine should admit its own lack of methods and incompleteness of knowledge, and treat patients with the attitude of "knowing what you know, and not knowing what you don't know." Patients can believe in both Chinese and Western medicine, but do not misunderstand the saying "Chinese learning as the core, Western learning for application" and make presumptuous claims to combine the strengths of both, because medicine is not a child's play, and the truth of the world is only one after all!

Plum Blossom

— Meng Hua

It is winter. According to the seasons, it is almost the time of "Heavy Snow". But in Shanghai, in the Jiangnan region, one can only see small snowflakes mixed in the "autumn rain" like cow's hair. At this time, I often miss the north, missing the pure white snow of the north.

Page 18

Early this morning, when I just woke up, the outside of the window was covered with a hazy white fog, and the sky was as gloomy as lead. I thought it was time for snow, but unexpectedly, after an hour or two, the sound of rain rang outside. Looking out the window, it was just like the weather in the late spring of the north, knowing that there was no hope of snow again. Living in this turbid city, we are too far, too far away from nature.

It is not because I have heavy fur coats or a warm home that I love snow. I get comfort from the snow. As soon as I see snowflakes flying in the air, I feel like I am in my hometown, and I feel satisfied. But now, it is raining outside, and I can't help but feel lonely.

In the rhythm of raindrops, the noise of the city is dull. Sitting in the cold room, I thought of what happened a few years ago.

It was on a clear morning after a heavy snowfall. When we got up and opened the window, we saw several inches of snow accumulated in front of the steps, and the roof was also covered with a white layer. So, Shu suggested to me, "Let's go to Beihai Park."

We walked towards Beihai Park, stepping on the snow. The white stone railings of the Jin'ao Yudong Bridge were covered with white snow, and the withered willows by the South China Sea pond were also dressed in new clothes. The frozen water surface of the Imperial River was evenly covered with a clean and soft white felt. On the snowy ground at the entrance of Beihai Park, our footprints were the first to be printed.

"Could it be that the plum blossoms are blooming!" Shu pointed to the trees covered with frost flowers in the distance and asked me. From where we were standing, it really looked like a plum forest full of white flowers.

"Really the tone of a southerner, where are there plum blossoms now? They are frost flowers!" I said.

We walked towards there, stepping slowly under the jade trees and jade branches. The snow under our feet made a low, crisp sound. From time to time, frost flowers and residual snow fell on our collars. We seemed to be surrounded by a misty sea of white flowers, and it seemed as if we had entered a quiet, cold fragrance.

Shu raised her hand and held onto a small branch. Just as she was about to break it off, she inadvertently shook off the snowflakes on the branches. What remained were the scorched yellow branches. She finally managed to break off a branch and gave it to me, saying:

"Beautiful. Next winter, we won't be here anymore. Maybe this is the last time, maybe after returning to the south, we will never see snow again. Let's keep this tender branch covered with frost flowers as a souvenir."

We looked at each other silently. I took the tender branch from her hand.

"You know, frost flowers are easy to disappear. They will melt in a short while."

She didn't answer, but looked up at me, her eyes filled with tears.

Now, in my luggage, I still treasure the tender branch she gave me, but since that time, we have left the north together and come to this prosperous Jiangnan. Jiangnan occasionally snows, but before October, she had quietly returned to her southern home.

Maybe she is waiting for the plum blossoms to bloom in the south, just as I am waiting for heavy snow. The snow should fall soon, but when will we meet again?

The rain is falling rustlingly outside the window, and my heart is even more lonely.

The Child Picking Up Trash

— Lu Zhi

Morning. When I took the book and walked out of the alley, a child walked towards me. He was very young, no more than three feet tall, wearing a single-breasted jacket in the style of a woman. I say "woman style" because the jacket was neither long nor short, just covering his knees. He wore a pair of foot-wrapped trousers, one gray and the other black broken rubber shoes, a melon-shaped hat turned inside out, carrying a broken burlap bag, and holding a pair of iron tongs for picking up trash. This is a common sight of poor children wandering the streets. He walked too solemnly, this unusual behavior of the child caught my attention, but I didn't pay attention. When he walked to a trash can not far from me, he stopped, tiptoed, and leaned half his body to climb into the trash can. A burst of dust flew up from the mouth of the can as he searched for what he needed.

After a while, he struggled to stand up, obviously disappointed. He straightened his bag, took the iron tongs and was about to walk to the second trash can. At this time, he very sincerely brushed away the dust on his dirty jacket. While brushing, he walked to the second trash can and picked up trash as before. He picked up something from the second can, stood up, and brushed his clothes as before, then turned and walked into the alley... A light, natural action that moved me very much.

The clothes were already very dirty, and he was going to continue climbing into trash cans, continuing to soil them. But he didn't give up brushing off the dust just because of this inevitable reason. He was not upset because of the past, nor disappointed by the future. There was dust now, and he still tried his best to brush it off. From this kind of behavior, I saw the greatness of human vitality.

The child is still ignorant of life, maybe his action was accidental, but isn't this the case for most people? They are not upset because of their past unhappiness, nor are they disappointed by whether the future can be improved. They are still working hard on what they should do, working hard to achieve the completeness that their ability can reach, even if they have already fallen into disappointment, they are still constantly working hard, isn't this the same as the child picking up trash brushing the dust off his dirty clothes?

I thought of what Kouchuan Baicun said in his book "Symbols of Melancholy": "The life force that never wants to solidify or stagnate, avoids compromise and surrender, and only seeks freedom and liberation, is always burning in the depths of the heart, whether consciously or unconsciously." It is this burning flame that prevents people from falling into the abyss of despair, and enables mankind to conquer nature and build society, right?

This child picking up trash is still young, so the only way he can improve himself is to brush off the dust on his body. But if he can maintain this spirit and not let it solidify and stagnate in his life, then he will definitely be able to surpass his current life, this is undeniable. Therefore, I saw a terrible devil's hand grabbing him from behind, stuffing him into a trash can full of filth, begging for a living all day long, killing him alive. This devil's hand is none other than the society he lives in, our society.

Looking at his dark, innocent hands, I secretly blessed him, hoping that he would use these hands to brush away the devil's hand that was grabbing him, which is also what I should do.

The power of life is precious in human beings, but how much life force is suppressed, harmed, and eliminated?

I bit my lip and walked out of the alley, the child was long gone.

Woodcutter's Song

— Liu Wang

In the early morning, a thick fog was permeating the rolling hills, like a broad white gauze belt, tightly wrapping the trees on the mountains. The sun had already climbed up from behind the mountains, so magnificent and so brilliant. The golden light threads, like thousands of feathered arrows, pierced through the fog and sent out metallic laughter to the world.

Liga, the young and lively girl in the village, at this time shouldered a slender carrying pole, skipping and running through the winding path obscured by the fog, and headed towards the mountain. The blue and white patterned homespun headscarf fluttered in the morning breeze, brave and handsome. The carrying pole often jumped off her shoulders, so she simply held it in her hand, waving it skillfully like a Jianghu street performer.

Except when it rained or snowed, Liga would always run to the small mountain in front of the village early in the morning to chop firewood. When the sun was about to move directly in the middle of the sky, and the blue-gray smoke was swirling from the thatched roofs of the houses in the village, her firewood would also be piled into two large piles. Tying them up with ropes, she would carry them home.

Recently, she had been getting up even earlier and was even happier doing this work. It turned out that she had met Yun Ge'er from the east village the month before. The two fell in love privately and used this early time, when people didn't pay much attention, as an opportunity for their secret trysts.

Along a yellow sand mountain road, Liga nimbly climbed up the mountain. When she reached the mountainside, she darted into the woods, letting the emerald green pine needles conceal her. She pushed aside the thorns and stepped to the [blank] colored [blank] side. In the [blank] grass, a spring quietly flowed. It shot through the grass piles, climbed over the stone chips, making a gurgling sound. Many black lizards were crawling on the stones. Liga stretched out her bare feet, and these small animals all slid over the back of her feet and flowed down the mountain.

Liga reflected her face in a deeper part of the stream, checking if there was still sleep in her long eyelashes, and then scooped up a handful of spring water and smeared it on her face. She looked at the beautiful homespun headscarf, nodded, and smiled. She loved this new headscarf that she had tied on today. She thought that when Yun Ge'er saw it, he would definitely praise it endlessly.

Waiting and waiting, Yun Ge'er was still not seen. The thick fog on the mountain had become thin and was about to be dried up by the sun. She felt a little agitated, her heart empty. Throwing the carrying pole into the spring water, she sat down on the rock and sang her love song. The singing was clear and loud, echoing in the valley.

"Chopping firewood requires a hazy sky,

Loving a girl should be in her young years;

Beneath the pine forest, there is a black rock,

Just right for us to sleep neck to neck..."

Singing, Liga herself felt a little shy, humming the last sentence in a low and weak voice. A burst of irrepressible tenderness went away with the flowing spring. Her face gradually turned red, and touching her cheeks, they were burning hot. She somewhat hated Yun Ge'er, why hadn't he come yet? He should understand the preciousness of time!

She thought: Maybe he is sick? But it was absolutely impossible for a body as strong as a lion to get sick, so maybe he was tied up by other important things? Thinking and thinking, Liga picked up the carrying pole again and walked out of the pine forest. She stood on the mountain path looking towards the foot of the mountain, but there was no sign of Yun Ge'er. There was a person walking up, she recognized her clearly, it was Sister-in-law Xiang Sheng, Yun Ge'er's neighbor.

As Sister-in-law Xiang Sheng got closer, Liga could no longer restrain her boiling enthusiasm, and hurriedly asked. At this time, she had completely forgotten her shyness.

"Sister-in-law, have you seen Yun Ge'er?"

"Yun Ge'er? He went to Mount Liang Laoye to chop firewood yesterday afternoon. Someone saw him and reported it to Liang Laoye. This morning, Liang Laoye ordered three militiamen from the town's security regiment to arrest him." Sister-in-law Xiang Sheng said, while looking at the listener with concern.

Liga didn't even say hello to Sister-in-law Xiang Sheng and ran madly down the mountain. The carrying pole was dragged, jumping on the rugged mountain road. The blue and white homespun headscarf, like a corner of a flag, fluttered in the wind.

Movie

Ao Enhong and Lu's Brothers Joint Aid to Sui Film Exhibition

Recently, the Daxin Company has been constantly holding various exhibitions, but they are all more focused on calligraphy and painting. Except for the previous exhibition by the Westerner Mr. Nibbs, the photography exhibition has been deserted for a long time. Unexpectedly, at the end of this year, the young photographers Ao Enhong and the Lu Fu brothers will hold a joint aid to Sui photography exhibition on the fourth floor of Daxin Company (dates are from the 19th to the 31st of this month) to end this year's art scene. And their film exhibition is also of a patriotic nature.

This time, the three of them have a total of more than 230 works, of which Ao Enhong's are the most, accounting for half of the total, and Lu Yu's are the least.

Ao Enhong's works mainly depict life and architecture in North China.

Page 20

Page 21

At this critical time in North China, looking at them increases melancholy. Ao's photography often captures the most important point with extremely simple scenes, using light strokes to create beautiful pictures. Among them, No. 2 "A Blow of Wind", and No. [blank]'s "Smoke and Rain Picture", an ancient pine standing alone complementing the vivid characters, the picture is clear and elegant, and it is also mounted into a vertical axis, antique, simply a famous painting of the Tang and Song dynasties. No. 99's "Eulogy" and No. 93 "Flying", have strong tones and unique styles. Other outstanding works include the portrait "White Clouds Like Running Water Years", which is meaningful, the still life "Little Birds on Branches Accompany Red Makeup", the life scene "Winnowing Wheat", and the architecture "White Pagoda Night".

Lu Fu's works are mostly satirical, with very appropriate titles, such as "The Result of Laziness" and "Face as Round as a Rich Man," etc., with a strong cartoon style. No. 154 "Moon in the East Window" has excellent lines and is full of poetry; others, such as [blank] Yu [blank] "Drinking Water and Thinking of the Source" and "Old Tree Across Autumn," are all considered masterpieces.

It is said that their method of aiding Sui is to donate half of the proceeds from the sale of their works to the front line. Such an act is naturally enthusiastic and commendable.

"Lofty Ambition" Theme Song

The Xinhua blockbuster "Lofty Ambition" is a work reflecting the "storm of the times," directed by Wu Yonggang, starring Jin Yan, Wang Renmei, Chen Juanjuan, Wang Jielong, Han Langan, and others. This film depicts the process of farmers being plundered, entirely based on a bloody record of real life. Under Mr. Wu's novel and lively treatment, it unfolds as nothing less than a shocking picture. The theme song "Pulling the Plow Song" in the play, sung by Jin Yan and Wang Renmei, is generous and passionate, full of the spirit of struggle, enough to inspire the audience's national consciousness. The lyrics are recorded below:

(A) Heiyo pull, (B) Heiyo pull, (A) Heiyo pull, (B) Heiyo pull, don't look back, don't look back, our hometown only has poverty and sorrow! The water has become a disaster for three thousand miles, and the county magistrate urges rent as if it were fire! Abandon home, heiyo, leave the village, heiyo, walk the world, heiyo, the vast land of the border provinces can still survive!

(A) Pull hard, (B) Pull hard, (A) No livestock, (B) No livestock, (A) Let’s carry the adopted son on our shoulders, (B) Let’s carry the rope on our shoulders, heiyo pull, heiyo pull, reclaim wasteland, heiyo, open up wilderness, heiyo, rely on our own hands, heiyo, walk forward with blood and sweat! Art China Recent News

Art China Company's special blockbuster of this year, produced by Yan Chuntang, written by Huang Mo, and directed by Fang Peilin, "Sequel to Incarnation Girl," has been in production for half a year, exhausting all efforts, and is now announced to be completed. It is scheduled to be released publicly in Shanghai on New Year's Day, and it will surely cause a sensation among the audience, with a special grand occasion.

"Sequel to Incarnation Girl" stars Yuan Meiyun, along with Lu Ming, Wang Naidong, Han Langan, Guan Hongda, Qin Tong, Wang Guilin, Liang Dusheng, and others, working together with outstanding talent and skilled acting, goes without saying. The film has beautiful writing, clear light, bright sound, and magnificent scenery, which is the fact that Art China dominates the silver screen. It is a sincere contribution after Christmas, and a blockbuster worth watching.
